201 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Slewett & Farber v. Board of Assessors etc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 547; 430 N.E.2d 1294; 446 N.Y.S.2d 241; 1982 N.Y. LEXIS 3039


November 18, 1981, Argued  
January 7, 1982, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, without costs, in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed. Question certified answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Board of Assessors of the County of Nassau and the Attorney General of the State of New York, Appellants, challenged a judgment of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which granted cross motions for reargument, vacated its prior decision and modified, on the law, and, as modified, affirmed an order of the trial court. A question as to the correctness of the order was certified.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers challenged tax assessments made on their property. The intermediate level court affirmed as modified a trial court order which, inter alia, declared portions of the state property tax law unconstitutional and set the applicable ratio at the rate determined by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment as the state equalization rate for the county. On appeal by the Board of Assessors and the Attorney General, the court held that the constitutionality of the statutes was not at issue, because the statutes expired during the pendency of the appeal. The court also held that the determination and assessment of the taxes entailed a bifurcated proceeding in which the appropriate ratio was first determined and thereafter the fair market value of the property would be assessed against which the ratio would be applied. The court held that the two-step process would determine the equality or inequality of the tax assessment made against the property. The court further held that the ratio determination was an interlocutory judgment that collaterally estopped the state from further challenging the rate in other proceedings.


OUTCOME: The appellate court judgment, which affirmed as modified a trial court holding as to tax assessments, was modified, without costs, and, as so modified, was affirmed. The question certified as to the correctness of the appellate court's decision was answered in the negative.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment -- State Equalization Rate

Subdivision 3 of section 720 of the Real Property Tax Law (L 1981, ch 1057), which effectively forecloses the use of State equalization rates as proof of unequal real property assessments in tax review proceedings in New York City and Nassau County, does not apply to proceedings in which the hearing with respect to assessment ratios was concluded and an interlocutory judgment was entered determining the rate of fractional assessment prior to December 3, 1981, the effective date of the new enactment, although the bifurcated tax review proceedings had not been concluded at that time. Accordingly, petitioners, real property owners in Nassau County who secured an interlocutory judgment prior to December 3, 1981 in a tax review proceeding wherein they challenged the assessments of their property as unequal, which judgment properly determined that the State equalization rates are appropriate proof of the rate of fractional assessment in Nassau County for the years in question, may proceed to prove that their property has been assessed in excess of that rate by establishing the property's fair market value, against which the predetermined fractional assessment rate will be applied; moreover, the validity of the State equalization rate having been adjudicated, the County of Nassau is collaterally estopped in other proceedings from further challenging that rate.

 

202 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Pharmaceutical Mfrs. Asso. v. Whalen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 486; 430 N.E.2d 1270; 446 N.Y.S.2d 217; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3207


November 19, 1981, Argued  
December 22, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, manufacturers of brand name drugs, a trade association comprised of such manufacturers, and an association of pharmacists, brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant state department of health, attacking the constitutionality of the Generic Drug Substitution Law. The trial court granted summary judgment to department, the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court (New York) affirmed, and plaintiffs sought review.


OVERVIEW: Under the Generic Drug Substitution Law, physicians can indicate that a generic drug be substituted for a more expensive "brand name" drug. N.Y. Educ. Law § 6810, subd. 6, par.(a). If a physician indicates that a generic drug should be substituted, a pharmacist is required to substitute a less expensive drug containing the same active ingredients, dosage form, and strength as the drug prescribed, as long as the substituted drug appears on the Department of Health's list of acceptable generic drugs.. N.Y. Educ. Law § 6816-a. The court agreed with the lower courts that the statute was constitutional. The court noted that where a police power enactment was challenged on due process grounds, the test was whether there was some fair, just and reasonable connection between it and the promotion of the health, comfort, safety and welfare of society; and that every legislative enactment enjoyed a strong presumption of constitutionality. The court concluded that the law was a reasonable exercise of the state's police power, and the law was rationally related to the legitimate purpose of safely reducing health care costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the appellate court, agreeing that the challenged law was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Drugs and Druggists -- Generic Drug Substitution

The "Generic Drug Substitution Law" (L 1977, ch 776), which requires that drug prescriptions signed by the prescribing physician on the "substitution permissible" line rather than the "dispense as written" line be filled with a less expensive equivalent drug if the product appears on a list of products prepared by the Department of Health (Education Law, §§ 6810, 6816-a) that have been certified or approved by the Federal Food and Drug Administration (FDA) as safe and effective for their indicated uses and for which there is no question of satisfying bioequivalency requirements (Education Law, § 206), is constitutional, since it is a reasonable exercise of the State's police power and is rationally related to the legitimate purpose of safely reducing health care costs; further, said law, which merely facilitates the exercise of the physician's responsibility to determine whether and under what circumstances generic drugs are to be prescribed, does not promote unfair competition or patent or trade-mark infringement, nor is it violative of due process, the commerce clause or any asserted patient-pharmacist "right to privacy".

 

203 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. De Jesus


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 465; 430 N.E.2d 1260; 446 N.Y.S.2d 207; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3205


November 16, 1981, Argued  
December 22, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with violating a city ordinance prohibiting the purchase of alcohol after hours, and the Monroe County Court (New York) entered a judgment that affirmed an order of the city court dismissing the information against defendants on the ground that the local ordinance, on which the prosecutions were based, was pre-empted by the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law.


OVERVIEW: The appeal required the court to determine the extent to which the State, by enactment of N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law ch. 478 had pre-empted the field of regulation of establishments that sold alcoholic beverages. The court found that the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law was pre-emptive because the regulatory system it installed was both comprehensive and detailed. Of particular relevance, it endowed the State Liquor Authority with the power to grant licenses under defined circumstances, and it provided for criminal sanctions against unauthorized purveyors of alcoholic beverages and carried its own provision against disorderliness being permitted on such premises. Moreover, the state's statutory structure imposed its own direct controls at the local level by creating local alcoholic beverage control boards. The court also found that a distinction argued by the State between the local and state regulations was not show. By dealing solely with the actions of patrons of establishments which sell alcoholic beverages, the ordinance impinged impermissibly on the exclusive Alcoholic Beverage Control Law.


OUTCOME: The order of the county court was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating Liquors -- State Pre-emption of Regulatory Field

The Alcoholic Beverage Control Law (L 1934, ch 478) is exclusive and State-wide in scope and, thus, no local government may legislate in the field of regulation of establishments which sell alcoholic beverages. Accordingly, criminal prosecutions based upon informations charging defendants, 125 patrons of an unlicensed "after hours" private club, with violating a local ordinance that prohibits any person from patronizing an establishment which is selling or offering for sale alcoholic beverages after 2:00 a.m., were properly dismissed; said ordinance impermissibly impinges upon the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law since it prohibits persons from patronizing such establishments at times when the pre-emptive State-wide scheme, which allows the sale of alcoholic beverages at retail for on-premises consumption until 4:00 a.m. (Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, § 106, subd 5), would permit them to do so.

 

204 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of XX


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 417; 430 N.E.2d 896; 446 N.Y.S.2d 20; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3167


October 20, 1981, Argued  
November 24, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner biological father sought review of the decision from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an order the trial court denying petitioner's application to vacate a prior order of adoption and denying petitioner's application to inspect the sealed records of the adoption.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner biological father sought review of the appeals court's decision affirming the trial court's denial of petitioner's application to vacate the adoption and denial of the application to inspect adoption records. Respondent mother and petitioner lived together prior to the birth of child. Respondent stepfather instituted a proceeding for his adoption of the child. Petitioner was served with a copy of the order to show cause and then learned for the first time of the pendency of the adoption proceeding. The trial court signed the final order of adoption. Petitioner sought to vacate the final order of adoption and to reopen the proceeding, which was denied by the trial court. On further appeal, the court rejected petitioner's assertions that the order of adoption should be set aside because respondents fraudulently concealed information from the trial court and because the trial court improperly waived a statutory prerequisite for adoption. The court concluded that there was no abuse of discretion when petitioner's application to reopen the adoption proceedings was denied. The court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeals court's decision affirming the denial of petitioner biological father's application to vacate the adoption and inspection of records because there was no abuse of discretion when petitioner's application to reopen the adoption proceedings was denied.


HEADNOTES

Adoption -- Notice to Putative Father

Neither the United States Supreme Court decision in Caban v Mohammed (441 U.S. 380), which, under certain circumstances, accorded putative fathers the right to veto a proposed adoption, nor its rationale, is applicable to an adoption proceeding that had been finally determined and concluded prior to the announcement of that decision. Further, it was not an abuse of discretion for the Family Court to grant a final order of adoption several weeks prior to the Caban decision without giving notice to petitioner putative father, of whose identity and interest the Judge had knowledge (Domestic Relations Law, §§ 111, 111-a), and, thereafter, to deny the application of the putative father to vacate the final order of adoption and to reopen the adoption proceeding (Domestic Relations Law, § 114); petitioner, who could have filed a notice of intention to claim paternity pursuant to section 372-c of the Domestic Relations Law and been assured the right to participate in the adoption proceeding (Domestic Relations Law, § 111-a, subd 2, par [c]), or promptly applied to intervene in the proceeding once he was aware of its pendency ( CPLR 401, 1012, subd [a]; 1013), did neither, and may not now obtain reversal of the final determination in an adoption proceeding to which he was not a party and in which all persons made necessary parties under the statutory and decisional law at that time were before the court and the only consent then required, that of the mother, had been obtained.

 

205 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Bellanca v. New York State Liquor Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 228; 429 N.E.2d 765; 445 N.Y.S.2d 87; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3125


October 15, 1981, Argued  
November 23, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: On reargument, following remand by the United States Supreme Court, judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court remanded respondent business owners' declaratory judgment action after determining that N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 106(6)(a), which prohibited topless dancing in establishments licensed by the state to sell liquor, was valid by reason of U.S. Const. amend. XXI.


OVERVIEW: The court found that § 106(6)(a), which prohibited all topless dancing in premises licensed by appellant N.Y. State Liquor Authority (state), was unconstitutional as a violation of U.S. Const. amend. I. The state appealed and the U.S. Supreme Court reversed the decision, finding that the statute was not unconstitutional because U.S. Const. amend. XXI gave to the state the power to regulate the times, places, and circumstances under which alcoholic beverages could be sold, which included the authority to ban the sale of liquor on premises where topless dancing occurred. The cause was remanded for further consideration and the court concluded that the statute was violative of the freedom of expression found in N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8. The court determined that the state constitutional provision was not subject to the curtailing effect of U.S. Const. amend. XXI. The court found that the exercise of the state's police power was necessarily subject to the strictures of the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court found the statute prohibiting topless dancing in establishments licensed by the state to sell liquor unconstitutional as a violation of the freedom of expression protected by the state constitution.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating Liquors -- Licenses -- Topless Dancing

Although the blanket proscription against topless dancing in premises licensed by the New York State Liquor Authority contained in subdivision 6-a of section 106 of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law is valid under the United States Constitution in consequence of the provisions of the Twenty-first Amendment, said categorical ban is invalid under the guarantee of freedom of expression declared in the New York State Constitution (art I, § 8), to which the Twenty-first Amendment has no application; however, the Legislature or the State Liquor Authority may, without infringement of the constitutional prescriptions, prohibit obscene dancing and may regulate, even to the extent of prohibition, nonobscene topless dancing in circumstances so functionally related to the exercise of the State's authority to regulate the sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages as to overcome the applicable constitutional protection of freedom of expression.

 

206 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Sibley v. Sheppard


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 320; 429 N.E.2d 1049; 445 N.Y.S.2d 420; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3158


October 12, 1981, Submitted  
November 19, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptive parents challenged an order from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which upheld a lower court's ruling that adoption did not extinguish respondent grandparent's rights to visitation and that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 72 did not amount to an invasion of the adoptive family's right of privacy such as would violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: The child lived with his maternal grandmother for several years before his mother died. After her death, he visited his grandmother frequently before ultimately being adopted by his paternal grandparents. The grandparent sought visitation of her grandson pursuant to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 72, but the adoptive parents argued that such visitation would violate their rights as parents established under § 117. The court upheld the visitation, finding that rights to parenthood were not beyond limitation. The court ruled that the state, through its police power, had the right to continue its supervision of the child's best interest, at least to the limited extent of allowing grandparent visitation where the birth parents were deceased. The court ruled that such a rule did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV because it was reasonably related to the goal of protecting the best interest of the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the appellate court, ruling that the grandparent was entitled to visitation of her grandchild, despite the adoptive parents' protests.


HEADNOTES

Adoption -- Visitation Rights of Natural Grandparents

Petitioner natural grandparent is entitled to visitation with her grandchild in accordance with the terms of a judgment issued pursuant to section 72 of the Domestic Relations Law granting her such visitation rights, based upon the court's determination that regular contact with petitioner maternal grandmother and her family, with whom the child had an established relationship, would be in the best interests of the child, despite the adoption of the child, whose natural parents are both deceased, and the protestations of the adoptive parents, and said relief is properly obtained in an action by writ of habeas corpus; the judgment did not effect an unconstitutional intrusion into the rights of the adoptive parents, who are the child's paternal grandparents (US Const, 14th Amdt).

 

207 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Greene


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 118; 429 N.E.2d 390; 444 N.Y.S.2d 883; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3074


September 8, 1981, Argued  
October 29, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York) that confirmed a referee's report finding appellant guilty of professional misconduct.


OVERVIEW: An attorney mailed fliers to real estate brokers to solicit business. A disciplinary agency's referee found that the attorney violated § 479 of the Judiciary law and Prof'l Responsibility Code DR 29-103(A). The finding was upheld by an appellate division, but no sanction was imposed. The attorney appealed. The grievance committee argued that the appeal should be dismissed as moot because respondent was suspended from the practice of law, on the basis of incapacity, and for lack of aggrievement in view of respondent's motion to confirm. The committee claimed that the record was not appropriate for decision, that the state interest sought to be protected was not sufficiently defined, and that his mailing was not an improper in-person solicitation. A lack of sanction did not foreclose an appeal. The court ruled that the provisions regulated the manner rather than the content of the commercial speech. Thus, because the regulations were reasonable in light of the governmental interest to prevent conflicts of interest in attorney-client relationships, the lack of effectiveness of the medium, and the more effective available alternatives, the statute was upheld as constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court judgment which confirmed a referee's finding that the attorney violated disciplinary rules.


HEADNOTES

Attorney and Client -- Advertising -- Direct Mailings to Real Estate Brokers

1. To the extent that section 479 of the Judiciary Law and DR 2-103(A) of the Code of Professional Responsibility proscribe advertising of attorneys' services by direct mail addressed to real estate brokers, those provisions regulate the manner rather than the content of commercial speech, and said proscription is reasonable in light of the governmental interest to be served, the lack of effectiveness of the medium and the availability of more effective alternatives. Accordingly, the restriction imposed by said provisions upon such commercial speech is constitutional; moreover, even were the proscription addressed to the content of the speech involved, it would still be constitutional, based on the substantial governmental interest in preventing conflicts of interest in attorney-client relationships that might arise from the intermediation of brokers.

Attorney and Client -- Disciplinary Proceedings -- Appeal

2. Respondent attorney's right of appeal from a confirmed finding that he violated the Judiciary Law and the Code of Professional Responsibility by direct mail advertising of his legal services to real estate brokers is not affected by the fact that no sanction was imposed upon him in a disciplinary proceeding, nor does petitioner's subsequent suspension from the Bar for incapacity render the constitutional question he raised to challenge the propriety of said finding moot, since the suspension, though indefinite in time, was made because of respondent's inability to participate in a formal hearing on new charges, from which incapacity he may recover; further, since the controversy is of a recurring character, it should not be dismissed for mootness.

Attorney and Client -- Code of Professional Responsibility

3. The Code of Professional Responsibility, an enactment of the New York State Bar Association, cannot, either directly or through incorporation in a court rule, amend or limit a statute adopted by the Legislature and, accordingly, to the extent that a code provision permits conduct by attorneys which is proscribed under the Judiciary Law, the statutory provision governs and operates to bar such conduct, unless the limitation imposed thereunder is found unconstitutional.

 

208 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Steinhardt v. Johns-Manville Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 1008; 430 N.E.2d 1297; 446 N.Y.S.2d 244; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3188


September 9, 1981, Argued  
October 29, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured parties and their estate representatives (injured parties), sought review of an order from the Supreme Court of Erie County (New York), which granted defendant tortfeasor's motion to dismiss and dismissed some of the injured parties' complaints. The injured parties also sought review of a separate order granting the tortfeasor's summary judgment motion and dismissing additional complaints filed by the injured parties.


OVERVIEW: Several injured parties filed personal injury actions seeking damages for the inhalation of asbestos particles during the course of the injured parties' employment. In some of the actions, the tortfeasor filed motions to dismiss the complaints, which the trial court denied. The appellate division reversed the trial court in those actions and granted the motions to dismiss and dismissed the complaints. From those dismissals, the injured parties appealed. In other actions, the tortfeasor filed motions for summary judgment, the trial court granted the motions, and the appellate court affirmed the trial court. The injured parties appealed from the grants of summary judgment. The court consolidated the appeals and affirmed the orders of the appellate court. The court held that each of the causes of action brought by the injured parties was barred by the statute of limitations of N.Y. C.P.L.R. 214-a, which began to run when each injured party inhaled the foreign substance, and expired after four years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's orders, which dismissed the injured parties' complaints.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions -- Strict Liability -- Negligence

In multiple actions seeking damages for injuries caused by the inhalation of asbestos particles by plaintiffs or their decedents during employment, where plaintiffs each commenced their action more than four years after the last employment-related exposure to asbestos, orders of the Appellate Division, which dismissed the complaints or affirmed orders dismissing the complaints, are affirmed. The cause of action in each case accrued at the time of the invasion of the injured party's body and not at the time the condition became apparent; further modification of this standard is a matter best reserved for the Legislature, and not for the courts.

 

209 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Svendsen v. Smith's Moving & Trucking Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 865; 429 N.E.2d 411; 444 N.Y.S.2d 904; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 3080; 32 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 275


September 8, 1981, Argued  
October 13, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed,  [***4] with costs, in a memorandum. Question certified answered in the affirmative.


HEADNOTES

Warehousemen -- Warehouseman's Lien -- Constitutionality

In an action for injunctive relief and a declaration that subdivision (2) of section 7-210 of the Uniform Commercial Code is unconstitutional, an order of the Appellate Division, which modified an order denying plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and class action certification, by granting the motion for summary judgment and declaring said statute unconstitutional, is affirmed for the reasons stated in the memorandum at the Appellate Division, which concluded that the statute violated the due process clause of the New York State Constitution (art I, § 6) since it authorized the ex parte foreclosure of a warehouseman's lien without affording the lienee the opportunity for a hearing, and by so doing the State had extended a creditor's rights beyond the common law and had so entwined itself into the debtor-creditor relationship as to constitute sufficient and meaningful State participation triggering constitutional protections, and that the procedure allowing ex parte foreclosure was a delegation to the warehouseman of the exclusive power [***5] of the sovereign to resolve disputes which was sufficient to involve due process protections.

 

210 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Bernstein v. Bodean


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 520; 426 N.E.2d 741; 443 N.Y.S.2d 49; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2670


June 8, 1981, Argued  
September 3, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, with costs to abide the event, and case remitted to Supreme Court, Nassau County, for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrator appealed from the order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed the trial court's jury verdict in favor of defendant physicians in the estate administrator's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was the victim of a rare malignancy which originated as a small growth on the left thumb and metastasized first to her arm and then to her lungs, eventually causing her death. The court held that the trial court impermissibly restricted the scope of the estate administrator's examination of two physicians who served on a medical malpractice panel which recommended that there was no liability on the part of the physicians. Thus, the jury verdicts in favor of the three physicians had to be set aside. The court held that the recommendation of the panel pursuant to N.Y. Jud. Law § 148a-8 was not intended to replace the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which was in favor of the physicians, and remitted for a new trial.


HEADNOTES

Physicians and Surgeons -- Medical Malpractice Mediation Panel -- Scope of Permissible Questioning of Physician Member of Panel

Following introduction in evidence of the recommendation of a medical malpractice panel concerning the question of liability, pursuant to section 148-a of the Judiciary Law, the doctor panel members called as witnesses may be examined, subject to the customary oversight of the Trial Judge, on any matter which will reasonably assist the triers of fact in assessing the probative worth of the panel recommendation. Any line of inquiry should be permitted which is found by the Trial Judge in the circumstances of the particular case not to be otherwise inadmissible and to be relevant and material to the assessment by the triers of fact of the evidential persuasiveness of the recommendation; examination shall not be permitted as to the qualifications of the panel member generally, but shall be exclusively focused on his qualifications related to and his participation in the panel recommendation; nor may he be asked to express opinions on hypotheses other than those before the panel. Accordingly, the trial court impermissibly restricted the scope of plaintiff's examination where it ruled that the panel physicians could testify on direct only as to the data made available to the panel and the procedures followed by the panel and not at to either their individual opinions or the basis for their participation in the panel's recommendation.

 

211 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gager v. White


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 475; 425 N.E.2d 851; 442 N.Y.S.2d 463; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2582


June 10, 1981, Argued  
July 7, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: In Gager v White: Order affirmed, with costs.

In Mei Yuet Chin v Cray: Order reversed, with costs, and the order of Supreme Court, Bronx County, reinstated.

In Cachat v Guertin Co.: Order affirmed, with costs. Question certified answered in the affirmative.

In Carbone v Ericson: Order reversed, with costs, and the order of Supreme Court, New York County, reinstated.

In Hill v Elliott: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) granted defendants' motions to dismiss, for lack of personal jurisdiction, plaintiffs' personal injury and wrongful death actions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs and their family members were residents of New York. Plaintiffs' family members were involved in automobile accidents outside New York with defendants, who were not residents of the state. Plaintiffs initiated various personal injury and wrongful death actions against defendants. Plaintiffs contended that jurisdiction lay in such courts pursuant to the Seider doctrine because defendants were insured by insurance companies authorized to do business in New York. Defendants filed motions to dismiss alleging that the New York courts did not have personal jurisdiction over them. Defendants contended that the Seider doctrine had been overruled by the Rush doctrine and the Rush doctrine was to be applied retroactively. Several courts dismissed for lack of personal jurisdiction, while several courts denied the motions to dismiss. On appeal, the court concluded that the Rush doctrine was to be applied retroactively. The Rush doctrine found that the principle announced in the Seider doctrine was violative of due process rights. The court concluded that the New York courts did not have jurisdiction over defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision because the New York courts did not have personal jurisdiction over defendants pursuant to the Rush doctrine.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Jurisdiction -- In Rem Jurisdiction

 Rush v Savchuk (444 U.S. 321), the effect of which declared the holding in Seider v Roth (17 NY2d 111) unconstitutional as violative of due process, Seider having held that a liability insurance contract issued by a carrier authorized to do business in New York can be attached and serve as the foundation for in rem jurisdiction over its nonresident insured defendants, is to be applied retrospectively only when a specific objection to the assertion of jurisdiction founded on the attachment of the out-of-State defendant's liability insurance policy had been preserved by appropriate motion or affirmative defense ( CPLR 3211, subd [e]); absent the pursuit of either of these courses, a defendant's voluntary participation in litigation in which the point can be raised constitutes a submission to the jurisdiction of the courts of the State and acts as a predicate for the basis jurisdiction.

First Colonie Co. v. Lyons


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 719; 426 N.E.2d 486; 442 N.Y.S.2d 992; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2650


June 12, 1981, Argued  
July 7, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, etc.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Application of State Sanitary Code's Fencing Requirement to Indoor Swimming Pool

An order of the Appellate Division, which reversed a judgment of the Supreme Court declaring portions of the New York State Sanitary Code (10 NYCRR 6.9 [a] [3], 6.16, 14-1.32 [b] [3]) valid and fully applicable to plaintiff's inn and granted judgment to plaintiff declaring that section 6.16 of the State Sanitary Code does not require that plaintiff's indoor pool be protected by a fence, is affirmed for the reasons stated in the memorandum thereat, which concluded that section 6.16 of the State Sanitary Code does not require that plaintiff innkeeper's indoor pool be fenced since the pool is protected by the building wherein it is located which is a compliance with the language of the statute.

 

213 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thomas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 338; 424 N.E.2d 537; 441 N.Y.S.2d 650; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2507


May 7, 1981, Argued  
July 6, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which reversed defendant's conviction, upon his conditional plea of guilty, of reckless endangerment in the first degree, criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree, and criminal possession of a weapon in the fourth degree.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant's convictions for reckless endangerment, criminal possession of a weapon, and criminal possession of a weapon were reversed, vacated, and remanded. Charges against defendant arose out of a high-speed car chase through a residential neighborhood. The court was required to determine whether a conditional plea was permissible. The court held that a defendant could not evade the consequences of a guilty plea by preserving legal issues for appeal. There was a logical inconsistency involved in permitting defendant to enter a plea of guilty and at the same time with the consent of the prosecutor and the approval of the court, obtain appellate review of the legal sufficiency of the evidence that would have hypothetically been adduced at trial to support conviction of the crime committed. Because defendant's pleas were conditioned upon the prosecutor's power to consent and the court's approval of such a plea and the plea would have been vacated if it was held that there was no such power, the court affirmed the appellate division's order. Defendant's pleas were vacated and the matter remitted for further proceedings on the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court ordering defendant's plea vacated and the matter remitted for further proceedings. Logical inconsistencies were involved in permitting a defendant to enter a guilty plea while obtaining appellate review of the legal sufficiency of the evidence.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Plea of Guilty -- Appeal

The legal sufficiency of a conceded set of facts to support a judgment entered upon a guilty plea may not be saved for appellate review by conditioning the plea on defendant's right to appeal that issue, even though the prosecutor consents to, and the Trial Judge approves, the entry of such a conditional plea; accordingly, because defendant's pleas were conditioned upon the power of the prosecutor to consent and the court to approve such a plea and provided for vacatur of the pleas if it was held that there was no such power, defendant's pleas are vacated and the matter is remitted for further proceedings on the indictment. The review of a legal issue concerning factual guilt is logically inconsistent with the principle that a plea of guilty is an admission of factual guilt.

Barber v. Dembroski


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

54 N.Y.2d 648; 426 N.E.2d 175; 442 N.Y.S.2d 768; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2609


June 9, 1981, Argued

HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Matters Reviewable

In an action by the Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets to recover assessments on apples made pursuant to the Agriculture and Markets Law, which would be used to sponsor advertising campaigns promoting apples, and which defendant apple growers refused to pay on the grounds that the assessments violated their [**3] rights of speech, assembly, equal protection and due process, and that they were improper delegations of the State's taxing and appropriating authorities, an order of the Appellate Division, which affirmed an order granting the commissioner's motion for partial summary judgment, dismissing the defenses and counterclaims, and directing the growers to take such measures as would allow a proper computation and payment of the assessments due, is affirmed, since the growers' contentions that the statute and implementing order violate the First Amendment of the United States Constitution and section 7 of article VII of the New York Constitution were not raised in their answer and thus are not reviewable in the Court of Appeals; the growers' other contentions are without merit.

 

215 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gold v. Gartenstein


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


54 N.Y.2d 627; 425 N.E.2d 892; 442 N.Y.S.2d 504; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2595


May 5, 1981, Argued  
June 18, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, etc.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Prohibition

In a proceeding to prohibit a Judge of the Criminal Court [**3] of the City of New York from enforcing his order declaring CPL 340.40 (subd 7) unconstitutional and directing a jury trial for a defendant who, as a first-time youthful offender, would not be entitled thereto under said statute, an order of the Appellate Division, which affirmed a judgment of the Supreme Court granting the writ of prohibition, is reversed, and the petition dismissed. It was error for Supreme Court to have entertained the application for article 78 relief in the nature of prohibition since that extraordinary remedy ordinarily may be employed only when a court acts or threatens to act without jurisdiction in a matter over which it has no power over the subject matter or where it exceeds its authorized powers in a proceeding over which it has jurisdiction; however, the instant determination is not an approval of the Judge's conclusion that the statute is unconstitutional, but merely a determination that the extraordinary writ of prohibition is an inappropriate means to address the claimed error in the ruling at Criminal Court in this instance.

Sinhogar v. Parry


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 424; 425 N.E.2d 826; 442 N.Y.S.2d 438; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2579


April 29, 1981, Argued  
June 18, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, without costs, in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed. Question certified answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties cross appealed from an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) which modified an order of the trial court in a class action for declaratory and injunctive relief relating to out-of-state placement of retarded foster children.


OVERVIEW: A class action for declaratory and injunctive relief and for damages was brought against defendant special services challenging the procedures to obtain judicial review of out-of-state placement of emotionally disturbed and mentally retarded foster children. The trial court determined, in part, that the procedures violated due process and special services sought review. The court affirmed; the procedures available met the requirements of both the Federal and State Constitutions since there was no constitutional mandate that notice and an opportunity to be heard be afforded prior to each out-of-state placement and the procedures available for postplacement review, which included administrative review in a fair hearing and/or judicial review in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, met constitutional due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order and affirmed; the court answered the certified question in the negative.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- Out-of-State Placement of Foster Care Children

The procedures presently available to both children and their parents to obtain judicial review of out-of-State placement of emotionally disturbed and mentally retarded foster children meet the requirements of both the Federal and State Constitutions; there is no constitutional mandate that notice and an opportunity to be heard be afforded prior to each out-of-State placement, and the procedures available for postplacement review, which include administrative review in a fair hearing and/or judicial review in a CPLR article 78 proceeding, meet constitutional due process requirements.

 

217 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Village Bd. of Fayetteville v. Jarrold


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 254; 423 N.E.2d 385; 440 N.Y.S.2d 908; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2479


May 5, 1981, Argued  
June 16, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent landowner appealed from an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Fourth Judicial Department (New York) that reversed a zoning board decision granting respondent's request for a use variance on real property.


OVERVIEW: Respondent landowner applied to the zoning board for permission to conduct commercial activity on his residentially zoned land. The zoning board granted a use variance based upon the finding that it would be economically unfeasible to build and attempt to sell a residential dwelling on the lot in question and granted a use variance. Petitioner then commenced a proceeding to invalidate the board's action. The lower court agreed and respondent appealed. The court affirmed the order denying the use variance because respondent failed to demonstrate factually, by dollars and cents proof, an inability to realize a reasonable return under existing permissible uses; therefore, a use variance could not be granted. The court held that conclusory witness testimony, unsupported by underlying concrete facts in dollars and cents form, provided no basis for a finding of unnecessary hardship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying respondent's request for a use variance because there was no concrete evidence of undue hardship and no dollar and cents testimony of respondent's inability to realize a reasonable return under existing permissible uses.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning -- Use Variance

A landowner who seeks a use variance must demonstrate factually, by dollars and cents proof, an inability to realize a reasonable return under existing permissible uses, and without such evidence, a grant of a use variance by a zoning board is not justified; accordingly, a zoning board improperly granted a use variance where respondent had applied for permission to conduct commercial activity on his residentially zoned land and presented conclusory testimony, unsupported and unsupplemented by underlying concrete facts in dollars and cents form, providing no basis to evaluate whether the property is being subjected to unnecessary hardship.

 

218 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Warder v. Board of Regents


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 186; 423 N.E.2d 352; 440 N.Y.S.2d 875; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2474


April 28, 1981, Argued  
June 11, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, proposed trustees of a seminary, sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court (New York) that affirmed respondent board's denial of a provisional charter to confer Master of Religious Education degrees.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, proposed trustees of a religious seminary, challenged respondent board's denial of a provisional charter to confer Master of Religious Education degrees. Petitioners alleged that respondent's determination should be annulled because it represented an abuse of the administrative process and a violation of petitioners' substantive and procedural rights. The lower court, finding no abuse of process, affirmed respondent's decision to deny petitioner's provisional charter. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court and held that summary judgment was properly granted in favor of respondent. The court found that the records submitted evidenced inadequate administration and that although petitioner explained certain inconsistencies, respondent was not bound to adopt the explanations as sufficient to dispel the impression of poor administration and conduct of the academic program. Moreover, the seminary failed to submit audited financial statements as requested. The court held that these deficiencies rationally could be considered contrary to the standards necessary for charter approval.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of petitioner proposed trustees' charter because there were no material factual issues raised by petitioners concerning respondent board's bias or abuse of the administrative process.


HEADNOTES

Colleges and Universities -- Denial of Charter to Theological Seminary

Summary judgment was properly granted dismissing petitions brought by the proposed trustees of a Seminary sponsored and financially supported by the Holy Spirit Association for the Unification of World Christianity, which challenged denial by the Board of Regents of the State of New York of a provisional charter application by said institution on the grounds that the decision was unreasonably delayed over the course of 30 months, despite initial reports in favor of approval by the Education Department and two independent consultants, and that the decision was arbitrary for numerous reasons, including bias, administrative abuse and the application of constitutionally vague statutory and administrative standards on the part of the board; at the very least, petitioners' school records evidenced inadequate administration and, by failing to submit audited financial statements, as requested, the Seminary failed to satisfy the board of its financial resources (Education Law, § 218), which deficiencies rationally could be considered contrary to the standards necessary for charter approval. The board had a right, following said initial, favorable recommendation, to delay its determination and to investigate serious allegations of illegal or unethical conduct, which inquiry is not rendered improper because said allegations were not ultimately sustained; moreover, petitioners were not denied due process, nor have they raised any material factual question concerning bias or an abuse of administrative process, and the statutes and regulations at issue offered sufficiently concrete guidelines and standards for judging an applicant to prevent the unfettered or arbitrary exercise of discretion.

Nussbaum v. New York City Employees' Retirement System


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

53 N.Y.2d 1018; 425 N.E.2d 869; 442 N.Y.S.2d 481; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2547

DISPOSITION: Order modified, etc.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits

In an action to declare section B3-36.6 (subd j, par [2]) of the Administrative Code of the City of New York unconstitutional in that it limited the amount of service credit which may be purchased by an employee in a superior optional pension plan for purposes of eligibility in such plan, thereby impairing plaintiff's contractual rights, an order of the Appellate Division, which modified an order denying plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and class action status, by granting a cross motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint, is modified by declaring the challenged legislation constitutional. Plaintiff was not unconstitutionally denied vested pension rights by legislation creating the additional, optional pension plan inasmuch as he executed a voluntary and knowing waiver of his rights under the superior plan when he withdrew therefrom; he could have remained in his existing plan without any of his rights being impaired and it was his decision not to do so that caused the alleged change in his rights; however, the Appellate Division should have declared the rights of the parties instead of dismissing the complaint.

People v. Haff


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 997; 424 N.E.2d 552; 441 N.Y.S.2d 665; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2532


May 5, 1981, Argued  
June 4, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed in a memorandum.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Freedom of Speech

1. Subdivision 3 of section 107 of the Civil Service Law, which proscribes the giving within a building occupied for governmental purposes by a public officer to his subordinates of notice that they are to collect and receive political contributions, is a valid regulation of partisan political conduct; limited as to place, its regulation of speech is reasonable, and, in view of the commonly understood meaning of the words in which it is phrased, it cannot be held void for vagueness.

Crimes -- Notice of Political Assessment

2. The Appellate Division properly affirmed a judgment convicting defendant of violating subdivision 3 of section 107 of the Civil Service Law by giving notice to subordinates, within a building occupied for governmental purposes, that they were to collect and receive political contributions. The evidence of defendant's guilt was sufficient, since the statute does not require that coercive language be used, and since there was nonaccomplice testimony fairly tending to connect defendant with the commission of the crime.

223 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Legal Aid Soc'y of Sullivan County, Inc. v. Scheinman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 12; 422 N.E.2d 542; 439 N.Y.S.2d 882; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2381


February 11, 1981, Argued  
May 12, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the counsel for defendant, appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which dismissed petitioner's N.Y. C.P.L.R. art 78 mandamus motion to compel relief under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 170.25.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in an information with disorderly conduct and resisting arrest. Petitioner, his counsel, moved a county judge under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 170.25 to remove the case to another court, to have the charges brought in an indictment, and to have the case presented to a grand jury. The judge denied the motion, and petitioner, in his name, brought a mandamus motion under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78. The motion was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. Although the court questioned the standing of petitioner to bring the motion, the court declined to dismiss upon those grounds. Mandamus, an extraordinary remedy, was inappropriate, thought the court, because defendant could not bring such an interlocutory action where alternatives existed to provide relief. Namely, the court found that review of a claim of deprivation of constitutional rights or appeal of a judgment of conviction would have been more appropriate measures in this case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the mandamus motion.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against Body or Officer--Mandamus

Relief under CPLR article 78 in the nature of mandamus does not lie to compel the removal by a superior court of charges pending in a local criminal court in order to assure a defendant trial before a lawyer-trained Judge, since mandamus lies to compel the performance of a purely ministerial act where there is a clear legal right to the relief sought, and the defendant can obtain full judicial review of his claim, that he was deprived of his constitutional rights when his application for removal was rejected, on direct appeal from any judgment of conviction against him.

 

224 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Teicher


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


52 N.Y.2d 638; 422 N.E.2d 506; 439 N.Y.S.2d 846; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2402


April 2, 1981, Argued  
May 12, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, by permission of a justice of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), from an order of the court, which affirmed defendant's conviction under N.Y. Penal Law § 130.65 of two counts of sexual abuse in the first degree following a nonjury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant dentist was convicted, under N.Y. Penal Law § 130.65, of sexually abusing two female patients, one of them a police officer, while they were under the effects of sedation in his office. Part of the evidence used to convict him came from a camera, which was placed in defendant's office, pursuant to a warrant. On appeal, defendant claimed that the evidence at trial was insufficient to establish that one of the patients was incapable of consent as per the statute. Defendant also claimed that introduction of the video recording was improper under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 700.05 and the federal wiretapping statute, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2516(2). The court affirmed the conviction. Section 130.65 did not require that actual gratification occur, only a touching for that purpose was sufficient. The warrant that permitted the seizing of an intangible visual image secured by a video camera was proper since it met all the requirements of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 690.10(4). The federal statute was not applicable to video recordings, and there was enough probable cause, particularization, and minimization presented to the warrant authority to have satisfied the constitutional standards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the appellate division, which affirmed defendant's conviction of two counts of sexual abuse in the first degree where the constitutional requirements in obtaining a warrant of a video recording camera had been met.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Eavesdropping Warrants -- Video Tape Recordings

1. A warrant may issue to authorize the video tape recording of evidence to be admitted at a subsequent trial; CPL article 690 is broad enough to include warrants for the seizure of intangible visual images ( CPL 690.10, subd 4). However, the requirements for aural electronics surveillance set out in Berger v New York (388 U.S. 41) and Katz v United States (389 U.S. 347) apply with equal force to video electronic surveillance: (1) there must be a showing of probable cause to believe that a particularly described person is committing, has committed or is about to commit a crime, that the place where the activity is to be intercepted is being used or is about to be used in connection with the commission of a crime by that described person and that a particular activity related to that crime will be observed through the use of the video electronic surveillance; (2) the warrant must be sufficiently particular, specifying the type of activity sought to be captured by the camera and the person expected to be seen performing the activity; (3) the warrant must provide that the surveillance be conducted in such a way as to minimize recordings not related to the specified crime under investigation, and (4) there must be no less intrusive means of obtaining the needed evidence.

Crimes -- Sexual Abuse

2. The crime of sexual abuse in the first degree, defined as subjecting another person to sexual contact, i.e., any touching of the sexual or other intimate parts of a person not married to the actor for the purpose of gratifying the sexual desire of either party (Penal Law, § 130.00, subd 3), when the other person is incapable of consent by reason of being physically helpless (Penal Law, § 130.65, subd 2), was made out where the defendant placed the victim's hand against his genital area, although this involves the victim touching the defendant rather than the reverse; further, such contact, while it was fleeting because the victim withdrew her hand, establishes the necessary element of sexual gratification as the purpose of the touching and, although the woman, who was heavily sedated when the original touching occurred, had enough control over her body to pull her hand away, the trier of fact was entitled to infer that she lacked capacity to consent to the touching because of her generally weakened condition.

Crimes -- Sexual Abuse

3. A police woman's consent to act as a decoy, placing herself in a situation where she was sedated and subjected to certain sexual touchings by defendant, who was subsequently convicted of sexual abuse in the first degree (Penal Law, § 130.65, subd 2), is not the equivalent of a consent to the touching of her intimate parts, which she was physically incapable of giving at the time of the illegal activity; moreover, the fact that the woman was able to tell defendant, in response to his direction that she stand, that she could not do so, but made no statement during the subsequent touchings, does not mean that the trier of fact could not find the necessary element of inability to consent to such touching due to physical helplessness required for conviction of said crime.

 

225 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ferber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


52 N.Y.2d 674; 422 N.E.2d 523; 439 N.Y.S.2d 863; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2405; 7 Media L. Rep. 1417


April 2, 1981, Argued  
May 12, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order revsered, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) affirmed defendant's conviction for promoting a sexual performance by a child, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 263.15. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold two films to an undercover police officer and was then convicted of promoting a sexual performance by a child, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 263.15. Before trial defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment on the ground that § 263.15 was unconstitutional. That motion was denied. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. On appeal, however, the court found that § 263.15 was unconstitutional. The court found that because N.Y. Penal Code § 263.10 prohibited the promotion of obscene sexual performances by children, N.Y. Penal Code § 263.15 must have prohibited only the promotion of non-obscene sexual performances by children. Otherwise, § 263.15 would have been meaningless. Thus, the court found that § 263.15 could have been applied to any play or movie in which a child portrayed a defined sexual act, real or simulated in a non-obscene manner. The court also found that it could reach educational materials or other non-obscene expression. Thus, the court found that the statute regulated content in violation of the First Amendment. The court found that no justification had been shown for such a restriction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, which had affirmed defendant's conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Promoting Sexual Performance by Child

 Section 263.15 of the Penal Law, which provides that "A person is guilty of promoting a sexual performance by a child when, knowing the character and content thereof, he produces, directs or promotes any performance which includes sexual conduct by a child less than sixteen years of age", is unconstitutional since it discriminates against films and other visual portrayals of nonobscene adolescent sex solely on the basis of their content, and no justification has been shown for the distinction other than special legislative distaste for this type of portrayal; the statute is not directed at obscene performances, which are proscribed by section 263.10 of the Penal Law, and would in many, if not all, cases prohibit the promotion of materials which are traditionally entitled to constitutional protection from government interference under the First Amendment.

 

226 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Collard v. Flower Hill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


52 N.Y.2d 594; 421 N.E.2d 818; 439 N.Y.S.2d 326; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2356


March 31, 1981, Argued  
May 7, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York) that dismissed their complaint for review of the defendant's denial of their application to enlarge structures on their property.


OVERVIEW: Previous owners of plaintiffs' property entered into covenant with defendant that no construction on the property was allowed without defendant's consent. This covenant was entered in exchange for an amendment to a zoning ordinance. Plaintiffs' later application to enlarge the structures on the property was denied by defendant. In their complaint for review, plaintiffs alleged that defendant's actions were arbitrary and capricious. At hearing, a decision was entered in plaintiffs' favor, but on appeal, plaintiffs' complaint was dismissed. Plaintiffs appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that while the conditions imposed by the covenant may be unreasonable, the covenant could not be challenged absent an allegation that defendant's actions were in bad faith. Further, absent a provision that consent could not be unreasonably withheld, the court would not compel consent.


OUTCOME: Decision dismissing plaintiffs' complaint affirmed on the grounds that plaintiffs' allegation that defendant's action was arbitrary and capricious did not amount to an allegation of bad faith, and court could not review plain language of covenant without allegation of bad faith.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning -- Conditional Rezoning

A village, which conditioned an amendment of its zoning ordinance on the execution of a private declaration of covenants by the landowners providing, in part, that no construction may occur on the property rezoned without the consent of the board of trustees, may not be compelled to issue such consent or give an acceptable reason for failing to do so absent a provision in said declaration that such consent could not be unreasonably withheld; the landowners do not contend that the adoption of the original resolution by the village board constituted impermissible spot zoning or that the action of the board at that time was otherwise unreasonable or constituted an impermissible exercise of its zoning powers, nor is the landowners' allegation that the village board acted in an arbitrary and capricious manner in denying their application for approval to enlarge and extend the existing structure on the premises an assertion that the board acted in bad faith or its equivalent.

 

227 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Loretto v. Teleprompter Manhattan CATV Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


53 N.Y.2d 124; 423 N.E.2d 320; 440 N.Y.S.2d 843; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2471


February 11, 1981, Argued  
May 7, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord brought an action against cable television providers, challenging the constitutionality of N.Y. Exec. Law § 828, which governed the installation of cable television facilities upon her property. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the providers. The appellate court affirmed. The landlord appealed.


OVERVIEW: A landlord purchased an apartment building. Thereafter, she began the instant class action against the providers on behalf of a class consisting of all owners of real property in the state of New York on which the providers had placed any cable television component. As to her own property, she alleged that a cable television cable had been placed on the roof to provide service to a first floor tenant. The landlord sought damages for the trespass and an injunction against its continuance. She alleged that the providers acted under the purported authority of N.Y. Exec. Law § 828 and that such actions constituted a taking without just compensation and a deprivation of property without due process of law. The court held that the statute, which required a landlord to allow installation of cable television facilities upon his property for the use of his tenants or the tenants of other buildings or both, was a valid exercise of the police power rather than a taking requiring compensation, notwithstanding that the statute permitted the payment by the cable television company for such installation of such amount as the state commission on cable television determined to be reasonable.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of the providers was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Trespass -- Installation of Cable Television Facilities -- Police Power

1. Section 828 of the Executive Law, which requires a landlord to allow installation of cable television (CATV) facilities upon his property for the use of his tenants or the tenants of other buildings or both, is a valid exercise of the police power rather than a taking requiring compensation, notwithstanding that the statute permits the payment by the CATV company for such installation of such amount as the State Commission on Cable Television determines to be reasonable; the purpose sought to be achieved is rapid development of and maximum penetration by a means of communication which has important educational and community aspects, which is a legitimate purpose for use of the police power, and the provisions of section 828 are reasonably and substantially related to that purpose. Neither the physical invasion of the landlord's property by the attachment of such facilities nor the fact that at the time the facilities are attached to a building no tenant of that building is a CATV subscriber invalidate the legislative exercise of the police power, in view of the minimal nature of the invasion and the absence of any reasonable expectation on the part of the landlord that the space thus utilized would ever be income productive.

Parties -- Standing

2. Plaintiff, who purchased in 1972 an apartment building which had had cable television facilities installed, has standing to maintain an action for a declaratory judgment concerning the scope of and constitutionality of section 828 of the Executive Law, which provides that no landlord shall interfere with the installation of cable television (CATV) facilities upon his property or premises, since that section, if applicable and valid, prevented her interference with the CATV facilities on her premises from and after the effective date (January 1, 1973) of the section. Additionally, plaintiff's transfer of the property to a corporation wholly owned by her did not cause the action to abate, since she was the real party in interest and the transfer occurred after the action was brought (see CPLR 1018).

Administrative Law -- Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies

3. Administrative remedies provided by a statute need not be exhausted prior to the bringing of an action which challenges the enactment in its entirety as unconstitutional; accordingly, in a declaratory judgment action in which plaintiff seeks a determination that because section 828 of the Executive Law grants a statutory license to the cable television company holding the franchise for her area to attach its equipment to her property, it is a facially invalid exercise of the police power and, if construed to be an exercise of the power of eminent domain, in that aspect as well, plaintiff need not first apply to the State Commission on Cable Television (9 NYCRR 598.2) for the fixation of a fee in excess of the $ 1 fee which the commission has stated is the nominal fee to which, generally, a landlord will be entitled.

Trespass -- Installation of Cable Television Facilities

4. In light of the declaration of legislative intent contained in article 28 of the Executive Law, the language of section 828 of the Executive Law considered in its entirety, the use in section 828 (subd 1, par a) of the word "facilities", and parts of the legislative history, the Legislature intended to proscribe interference by any owner of rental property with the installation of cable television (CATV) facilities on his property whether used to furnish service to the tenant or tenants of the property on which installed or of another property or properties or both, but to permit such an owner to demand payment only from the CATV company making the installation and only for the service extended to tenants of his own property.

 

228 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Hardenburgh v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


52 N.Y.2d 536; 421 N.E.2d 795; 439 N.Y.S.2d 303; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2351


February 11, 1981, Argued  
April 30, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: On appeal by the town and town officials: Appeal dismissed, without costs.

On appeal by the remaining plaintiffs: Order modified in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed, with costs to defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, town and town officials suing in both their individual and official capacities, challenged the decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which dismissed the complaint as to town officials for lack of standing, adjudged N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 436 as valid and constitutional, and denied the cross motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: A town and its officials commenced a declaratory judgment action on behalf of those property owners residing in the town who claimed they would be entitled to a religious property tax exemption under § 436, but who, under an amended wording, were not able to qualify for the exemption. The court dismissed the town officials from the action because a substantial constitutional question was not directly involved. The town and officials failed to show that the statute did not apply evenhandedly to various religious groups, nor show that the statute interfered with any particular religious practice or belief. The statute merely imposed a reasonable regulation on the manner in which property eligible for the religious exemption was held, and where the state had a significant interest in distinguishing church property employed for the benefit of the church from that diverted to private or nonreligious use.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the state was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Court of Appeals -- Appeal as of Right

1. In a declaratory judgment action brought by a town and various town officials in their official capacity on behalf of property owners who claim they would be entitled to a religious property tax exemption under section 436 of the Real Property Tax Law as worded prior to January 1, 1979, but who, under the amended wording, are now unable to qualify for exemption, in which action the Appellate Division agreed with the Supreme Court and held that the plaintiffs were without standing, an appeal to the Court of Appeals taken purportedly as of right is dismissed since a substantial constitutional question is not directly involved; the basis of the Appellate Division's affirmance of the dismissal of the complaint was not on the merits of the First Amendment challenge, but rather on consideration of the standing of the parties to bring the suit, and accordingly, the asserted constitutional issue was not a basis of the decision below.

Taxation -- Exemptions

2. In a declaratory judgment action brought on behalf of property owners who claim they would be entitled to a religious property tax exemption under section 436 of the Real Property Tax Law as worded prior to January 1, 1979, but who, under the amended wording, are now unable to qualify for exemption, chapter 738 of the Laws of 1978, which amended section 436 effective January 1, 1979, is declared constitutional insofar as it affects the case, since there is no showing that the statute, which now requires that church officers hold the property in trust as a clergyman or minister in order to qualify for exemption, does not apply evenhandedly with regard to various religious groups, nor have plaintiffs shown any particular religious practice or belief with which the statute interferes.

 

229 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


State Bd. of Equalization & Assessment v. Kerwick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


52 N.Y.2d 557; 421 N.E.2d 803; 439 N.Y.S.2d 311; 1981 N.Y. LEXIS 2353


February 11, 1981, Argued  
April 30, 1981, Decided



DISPOSITION: In each case: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA), brought an action against respondent assessors to enforce its order that certain real property be restored to nonexempt assessment rolls. The assessors motion challenging the orders was dismissed and the SBEA's motion was granted. The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York) reversed the trial court and the SBEA appealed.


OVERVIEW: The assessors claimed that the SBEA did not have the authority to engage in an effort to prevent the exemptions. The SBEA claimed that it had statutory authority in N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 202 to compel adherence to its instructions through immediate judicial proceedings without the necessity to comply with the review procedures set forth in N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 216(2). The court held that the SBEA went beyond its intended scope of procedural regulation. The court found that the essential function of the SBEA was to advise on assessment matters, to keep current equalization rates, and to aid in the assessments, but that there was no authorization to direct substantive assessment decisions. The SBEA was seeking to go beyond its intended scope of procedural regulation. The SBEA's effort to prevent exemptions was beyond its general supervisory function, and the statutes contained no authorization for substantive input much less control by the SBEA in the individualized local assessment process.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate division that the SBEA had gone beyond its jurisdiction was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment -- Powers of Board of Equalization and Assessment

1. The petition is dismissed in a proceeding brought by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA) after the respondent assessor's wholesale grant of exemptions from real property taxation to members of the Universal Life Church, seeking a declaration that the 1977 tentative assessment roll is void, to enjoin certain respondents from taking any action to establish the tentative assessment roll as the final assessment roll for 1977, and directing the assessor to restore to the taxable portion of the tentative assessment roll all real property granted exemptions in an arbitrary, capricious or unlawful manner, in view of the SBEA's failure to comply with section 216 of the Real Property Tax Law; although section 202 (subd 1, par [g]) of the Real Property Tax Law provides that the board shall furnish assessors with such information as may be necessary or proper to aid them in making assessments, which instructions shall be followed and compliance with which may be enforced by the board, subdivision 2 of section 216 of the Real Property Tax Law provides that whenever any assessor has failed to comply with any rule or regulation of the board, after a hearing the board may direct such assessor to comply and following failure to comply the board may apply to a Justice of the Supreme Court for a summary order of compliance.

Taxation -- Assessment -- Powers of Board of Equalization and Assessment

2. The State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA), which is possessed of general supervision of the function of assessing (Real Property Tax Law, § 202), is not authorized to direct substantive assessment decisions and may not hold hearings or institute court proceedings in an attempt to obtain compliance with its view as to exemptions from real property taxation granted to members of the Universal Life Church.
