Zubli v. Community Mainstreaming Associates, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 1024; 410 N.E.2d 746; 431 N.Y.S.2d 813; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2926


June 5, 1980, Argued  
July 3, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Modified.


HEADNOTES

Mental Health -- Licensing of Community Residential Facilities -- Constitutionality of Statute

In an action for injunctive relief and to declare unconstitutional section 41.34 of the Mental Hygiene Law, which provided for the establishment and licensing of community residential facilities for the mentally disabled, an order of the Appellate Division, which affirmed a judgment of [**3] Special Term granting defendants' motion for summary judgment, is modified, by declaring section 41.34 constitutional as applied, and, as modified, affirmed, for the reasons stated in the opinion at Special Term, which concluded that the statute did not effect an unconstitutional taking of plaintiffs' property without due process or just compensation by permitting the establishment of a facility on property adjoining that of plaintiffs, and that the statute was not an unconstitutional exercise of local zoning authority by the State but instead was a valid exercise of the police power.

 

248 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shapiro


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 747; 409 N.E.2d 897; 431 N.Y.S.2d 422; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2466


April 24, 1980, Argued  
July 3, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and case remitted to Westchester County Court for further proceedings on the indictments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which modified, and as modified, affirmed a trial court judgment convicting defendant of promoting prostitution in the first degree, two counts of endangering the welfare of a child, sodomy in the second degree, and 11 counts of sodomy in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on a consolidated indictment of promoting prostitution in the first degree, endangering a minor's welfare, and sodomy in the second and third degrees. The appellate division reduced the sentence but affirmed the conviction. On appeal, defendant claimed abuse of discretion by the trial court when it denied his motion to sever the indictments, violation of his due process rights because the prosecution threatened his witnesses with perjury if they testified on defendant's behalf after exercising the self-incrimination privilege, and invalidity of the eavesdropping orders because they exceeded the bounds set by the federal wiretapping statute, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2516. The court reversed the conviction and ordered a new trial. The trial court's failure to weigh relevant and critical considerations during the motion to sever was an abuse of discretion. The prosecution's refusal to extend immunity to the witnesses and his perjury threats violated defendant's due process rights. N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 700.05 contravened the requirements of 18 U.S.C.S. § 2516. The wiretaps were invalid and the evidence stemming from them should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The order of the appellate division was reversed and the case remitted because the trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's motion to sever the indictments. Additionally, the wiretaps were illegal and the evidence obtained from them should have been suppressed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Indictment -- Improper Joinder of Indictments

1. It was an abuse of discretion as a matter of law ( CPL 200.20, subd 3) for the trial court to deny defendant's motion to sever an indictment embracing a total of 64 criminal counts charging him with engaging in a course of homosexual sodomitic acts on various occasions over a 17-month period with eight different boys under the age of 17, who received money from the defendant therefor, from his trial on two other indictments charging him with the more serious crime of promoting such conduct, which allegations were confined to a single incident and involved two other boys under 17 years of age, where there was no physical evidence that any act of sodomy had been completed with the boy with whom defendant was found at the time the police arrested him for promotion, no one figuring in the first indictment other than the defendant would have any reason to be called at the trial on the other indictments, and defendant, who did not plan to take the stand at the trial on the first indictment, desired to do so at the trial of the promotion charges; since prosecutions for sex crimes, particularly ones regarded as deviate, tend in any event to invoke prejudicial preconceptions among jurors, and in light of the dearth of physical evidence on the promotion charges, the joinder of the separate sets of charges created an impermissible risk that defendant would be convicted on the promotion counts for reasons other than those legally relevant to the specific crimes charged and the joinder also added impermissibly to defendant's choice in deciding whether to take the stand in his own defense and bear the risk on both sets of charges, although he might benefit on only the one.

Crimes -- Immunity from Prosecution

2. One who is granted immunity in return for his testimony receives no license to swear falsely with impunity while under the protection of that immunity.

Crimes -- Fair Trial -- Prosecutorial Misconduct

3. Although a District Attorney has an obligation to warn potential witnesses of their possible liability for false statements made under oath, such warnings must not be emphasized to the point where they become instruments of intimidation, nor may the refusal of a witness to testify due to fear of a perjury prosecution, which refusal results in the withholding of relevant testimony, be justified on the presumption that the witness in question will swear falsely; moreover, in cases in which witnesses favorable to the prosecution are accorded immunity while those whose testimony would be exculpatory of the defendant are not, or in ones where the failure to grant immunity deprives the defendant of vital inculpatory testimony, due process may be violated. Accordingly, where, when confronted with repeated threats by the prosecution that their testimony for defendant would result in prosecutions for perjury if it was at all different from previous testimony given at other, related trials and Grand Jury proceedings, three of defendant's witnesses invoked the privilege against self incrimination to protect themselves from said possible perjury prosecutions, each refusing to testify unless first given immunity by the prosecution, the District Attorney's refusal to extend immunity and the menacing terms in which he did so impermissibly affected the witnesses' meaningful exercise of their Fifth Amendment rights and denied defendant due process, which prejudice was not lightened when the Trial Judge refused to instruct the jury on the reason the witnesses were not called to the stand; the only way in which the prejudice created by the prosecutor's threats can be dispelled is to require that the witnesses for the defendant be granted immunity as a condition to subjecting the defendant to a new trial.

United States -- Federal Pre-emption -- Electronic Surveillance

4. Under pre-emption principles, any State law drawn more broadly than the Federal Omnibus Crime Control and Safe Streets Act of 1968, which imposes upon the States the minimum constitutional criteria for electronic surveillance legislation, runs afoul of the supremacy clause (US Const, art VI). Accordingly, to the extent that CPL 700.05 was read to permit wiretapping of defendant's home, which yielded evidence later used in connection with sodomy and promotion of prostitution charges, crimes involving persons less than 17 years old, but not involving any force, it contravened the requirements of subdivision (2) of section 2516 of the Federal statute (US Code, tit 18), which carefully enumerates the crimes considered serious enough to warrant investigation by wiretap, i.e., murder, kidnapping, gambling, robbery, bribery, extortion, or dealing in narcotic drugs, marihuana or other dangerous drugs or other crimes dangerous to life, limb or property, and the evidence gleaned therefrom should have been suppressed; that State law deems a person less than 17 years of age incapable of consent (Penal Law, § 130.05, subd 3, par [a]) does not catapult these otherwise consensual criminal acts into the status of crimes dangerous to life or limb.

 

249 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Nicholson v. State Com. on Judicial Conduct


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 597; 409 N.E.2d 818; 431 N.Y.S.2d 340; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2459


April 23, 1980, Argued  
July 1, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, with costs to the State Commission on Judicial Conduct, in accordance with the opinion herein, and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a candidate, campaign manager, and campaign workers, appealed the decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), denying the candidate's request for a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to enjoin further investigative proceedings by defendant Commission on Judicial Conduct. Respondent commission filed a cross-appeal challenging the order to seal the record.


OVERVIEW: In response to complaints of judicial impropriety that were filed against petitioner judicial candidate, respondent Commission on Judicial Conduct initiated an investigation. Petitioner candidate filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to enjoin further proceedings by vacating the complaint, quashing the subpoenas, and voiding her appearance. The court held that the commission had the right to investigate complaints brought to it. Petitioners claimed that the investigation would chill the rights of political expression. The court held that freedom of speech and association was an argument to be brought in defense of any action recommended and taken, but were not applicable at the investigative stage. The state's interest in preventing even the appearance of corruption outweighed any encroachment on petitioners' constitutional rights. The court then ruled that there was nothing in the statute that authorized the sealing of the court records. The confidentiality afforded in N.Y. Jud. Law § 44 applied to commission proceedings only. It was up to the legislature to create a blanket rule allowing for sealed records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision dismissing petitioner's request for prohibition to stop the investigation of impropriety in petitioner's campaign, but reversed the ruling to seal the court records, as there was no statutory authority against disclosure of the records.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Prohibition

1. Invocation of the extraordinary remedy of prohibition is appropriate only when there is a clear legal right and only when a body or officer acts or threatens to act without jurisdiction in a matter over which it has no power over the subject matter or where it exceeds its authorized powers in a proceeding over which it has jurisdiction; the remedy is available to prevent only judicial or quasi-judicial action, and it may not be sought to control merely legislative, executive or administrative acts. Even when the petition presents a "substantial claim" of an absence of jurisdiction or an act in excess of jurisdiction, prohibition still may be deemed inappropriate after consideration of such factors as the gravity of the harm which would be caused by an excess of power or whether the excess of power can be adequately corrected on appeal or by other ordinary proceedings at law or in equity, and prohibition is not available to correct mere errors of law, procedural or substantive, in litigation, but is, rather, the means to prevent an arrogation of power in violation of a person's rights, particularly constitutional rights.

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Prohibition -- Investigation by State Commission on Judicial Conduct

2. A CPLR article 78 proceeding in the nature of prohibition may be entertained where it is claimed that an investigation by the Commission on Judicial Conduct, which is vested with authority to investigate improprieties by members of the judiciary (NY Const, art VI, § 22), has a chilling effect on the exercise of First Amendment rights, and the claim seeks to vindicate rights of political expression and association long cherished in our constitutional scheme; if indeed the investigation impermissibly chills the exercise of these rights, the commission would be acting in excess of power and prohibition would be the appropriate remedy. The fact that the issues could be raised on appeal from any disciplinary action taken is not a persuasive reason for denying the availability of the remedy.

Judges -- Investigation by State Commission on Judicial Conduct

3. The investigatory activities of the Commission on Judicial Conduct, the body charged with policing the conduct of Judges, must be examined in light of the State's overriding interest in the integrity and impartiality of the judiciary, and the commission, when aware of acts which may constitute misconduct, must be free to conduct an investigation, which may touch upon political and associational rights, to determine whether formal charges are warranted; any First Amendment implications are far outweighed by the State's interest in the integrity of its judiciary. Accordingly, the First Amendment does not preclude an investigation by the commission of a complaint alleging that in connection with her 1977 campaign, a Surrogate engaged in and attended fund-raising activities, acquainted herself with the identities of her contributors and otherwise improperly participated in the campaign, that cash contributions in excess of $ 100 were accepted and expenses and contributions were not properly reported, and that the Surrogate exercised her power of appointment on the basis of favoritism and not solely on the basis of merit, in order to determine whether the filing of formal charges of misconduct is warranted; the compelled disclosure sought by the commission in the form of details of the campaign activities does not impermissibly impinge upon the free exercise of associational rights protected by the First Amendment, since there is a relevant correlation or substantial relation between the governmental interest and the information required to be disclosed in that comprehensive statutory disclosure requirements for political contributions and expenditures are justified by the governmental interests in providing the electorate with information about the source of funds and manner of expenditures, in deterring actual corruption and its appearance, and in detecting violations of permissible restrictions on the conduct of the campaign.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Political Expression -- Interference by State

4. Although the rights of political expression and association are at the heart of the First Amendment, not every interference with these rights violates the constitutional command; even significant restrictions on protected First Amendment rights may be sustained if the State demonstrates a sufficiently important interest and employs means closely drawn to avoid unnecessary abridgment of association freedoms. A proper analysis calls for examination of the degree of interference with the First Amendment interests, the strength of governmental interest justifying the restriction and the means chosen to prevent the asserted evil.

Witnesses -- Subpoena -- Authority of Investigating Body

5. A motion to quash or to compel compliance with a subpoena raises only the issues of authority of the investigating body and whether the inquiry falls within the scope of that authority.

Witnesses -- Subpoena -- Judges -- Investigation by State Commission on Judicial Conduct

6. Subpoenas issued by the Commission on Judicial Conduct, which is authorized to investigate complaints with respect to the conduct and qualifications of Judges and which may determine that a Judge be admonished, censured or removed for misconduct in office or conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice (NY Const, art VI, § 22, subd a; Judiciary Law, §§ 41, 42, 44), to a Surrogate's former campaign workers seeking information concerning allegations of improper campaign activities in connection with the Surrogate's 1977 election campaign, must be obeyed, since so long as the commission, in good faith, is investigating the conduct of a Judge, the commission is acting within the scope of its authority and a subpoena issued pursuant thereto is not subject to challenge; a witness called before the commission may not go beyond this inquiry to avoid compliance by attacking the specific allegations upon which the investigation is based.

Witnesses -- Subpoena -- Judges -- Investigation by State Commission on Judicial Conduct

7. In order to sustain subpoenas issued by the Commission on Judicial Conduct in connection with an investigation of judicial impropriety, the commission need only make a preliminary showing that the information sought is reasonably related to a proper subject of inquiry, and it is of no concern to a mere witness whether the commission is in possession of sufficient information to warrant the institution of formal proceedings; to require the commission to come forward with facts that would support a formal charge would be to restrict unnecessarily the commission's power to inquire into judicial misconduct, and such a requirement would render the commission ineffective as the instrument through which the integrity of the judiciary is assured.

Judges -- Investigation by State Commission on Judicial Conduct -- Sealing of Records

8. In a proceeding brought to enjoin an investigation by the Commission on Judicial Conduct into alleged improper campaign practices by a Surrogate, the Appellate Division improperly ruled that the legislative scheme of confidentiality for commission proceedings required sealing of the court records, since although the Legislature established strict rules of confidentiality to prevent premature disclosure (Judiciary Law, §§ 44, 45), the scheme applies only to matters before the commission and nothing in the statute can be read as applying to matters brought before the court; the public policy of the State is to ensure awareness of judicial proceedings, and while in an appropriate case a court may draw on its power to seal its own records, a blanket rule requiring the sealing of all court records involving proceedings by the commission is unjustified in the absence of legislative mandate.

 

250 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Press v. County of Monroe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 695; 409 N.E.2d 870; 431 N.Y.S.2d 394; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2463


May 30, 1980, Argued  
July 1, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant county, alleging that certain tax assessment rolls were void because the underlying rate schedule was unconstitutional. The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court (New York) dismissed the action on the basis that it was barred by the statute of limitations applicable to N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 78 actions, being N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 3211(a)(5). The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county had adopted a rate schedule that treated apartment complexes different than other units. The taxpayers, who owned an apartment complex, challenged assessments made in three prior years. Each of the prior years' assessments had been affirmed and adopted by the county, pursuant to N.Y. County Law § 271. In determining the applicable statute of limitations, the court noted that the taxpayers could have brought an action to review the assessments in each year that the assessments were made under N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 78. As the action was not commenced within the limitations period applicable to § 78 proceedings, being N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211(a)(5), the action was time-barred. In so ruling, the court noted that the taxpayers' constitutional challenges to the assessments could have properly been brought under N.Y.C.P.L.R. § 78. The adoption of the assessments by the county was not a legislative action. No statutory provision was enacted and no action was taken which would have had any carry-over effect beyond the particular assessment year.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate division.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions -- Action to Declare Sewer District Assessment Rolls Invalid

1. An action to declare invalid the assessment rolls of a sewer district as affirmed and adopted by a county legislature on the ground that the underlying rate schedule was unconstitutional is time-barred unless instituted within four months after such affirmation and adoption; accordingly, an action commenced by the owners of an apartment complex in 1978 seeking a declaration that the 1973, 1975 and 1976 assessment rolls were void by reason of the unconstitutionality of the underlying rate schedule which treated apartment complexes differently from other dwelling units within a sewer district is dismissed as time-barred, since the applicable Statute of Limitations is the four-month statute ( CPLR 217) because the controversy should more properly have been resolved in a CPLR article 78 proceeding to review each determination of the county legislature when it affirmed and approved the assessment roll of the sewer district for each particular year; the circumstance that the action sought to be reviewed is that of a legislative body does not stamp that action as "legislative" for purposes of determining whether challenges to the constitutionality of its action may be raised by means of an article 78 proceeding or whether recourse must necessarily be had for such purpose to an action for a declaratory judgment. The action of the county legislature sought to be reviewed was not "legislative" in the precise sense of that term, since the action in each year was taken by adoption of a resolution, not enactment of a local law, and no action was taken which would have any carry-over effect beyond the particular assessment year; furthermore, the underlying property classification plan to which plaintiffs directed their constitutional attack was not itself adopted or enacted, and to permit taxpayers to defer their challenges for a period of several years would be to expose the fiscal planning of the municipal unit to the risk of wholly unacceptable retroactive disruption.

Limitation of Actions -- Which Statute of Limitations Governs

2. In order to determine whether there is a limitation prescribed by law for a particular declaratory judgment action the substance of the action must be examined to identify the relationship out of which the claim arises and the relief sought; if that examination reveals that the rights of the parties sought to be stabilized in the action for declaratory relief are, or have been, open to resolution through a form of proceeding for which a specific limitation period is statutorily provided, then that period limits the time for commencement of the declaratory judgment action.

Actions -- Form of Action

3. A CPLR article 78 proceeding is not the proper vehicle to challenge the constitutionality of legislative enactments, although in most cases the application of this principle is of no practical significance inasmuch as the courts, in reliance on CPLR 103 (subd [c]), may remedy any procedural infirmity by converting the article 78 proceeding to a declaratory judgment action or other appropriate proceeding and then proceed to the merits.

 

251 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rosano


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 1013; 409 N.E.2d 1357; 431 N.Y.S.2d 683; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2538


May 27, 1980, Argued  
July 1, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed in a memorandum.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff and defendants appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York) that affirmed the conviction of defendants of larceny under N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a, and misappropriating trust funds and public offering of securities fraud in violation of N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law §§ 352-c, 352-e, 359-g, and 352-h.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with a 224-count indictment alleging criminal misconduct out of an uncompleted development project. Defendants were found guilty of 15 counts of larceny in violation of N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a, 4 counts of making a sworn false statement in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 210.35, 1 count of violating N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law §§ 352-c, 352-e, and 359-g with a public offering of securities, and 1 count of violating N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law §§ 352-h and 359-g for misappropriating trust funds. The appellate court reversed as to the false sworn statement conviction only, and all parties appealed. The court affirmed the reversal of the false sworn statement conviction since the evidence did not demonstrate beyond a reasonable doubt that the affidavits submitted to the lending institution constituted a falsity. The court also ruled that N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a(3) was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the appellate court was affirmed because the evidence failed to demonstrate that defendants submitted false affidavits to the lending institution and the law pertaining to larceny was not unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Larceny -- Misappropriation of Trust Funds -- Making Apparently Sworn False Statements -- False Representations in Offering Statements

1. An order of the Appellate Division which modified judgments convicting defendants of larceny in violation of section 79-a of the Lien Law, making apparently sworn false statements in the second degree, violating sections 352-c, 352-e and 359-g of the General Business Law in connection with a public offering of securities, and violating sections 352-h and 359-g of the General Business Law relating to misappropriating trust funds, by reversing the convictions of making apparently sworn false statements and otherwise affirmed, is affirmed essentially for the reasons stated in the opinion at the Appellate Division, which concluded that the disbursements of building loan contract funds and funds advanced by contract vendees of condominium units to the individual defendants and to corporations controlled by them were improper disbursements for nontrust purposes under section 79-a of the Lien Law; that although the defense of repayment under section 79-a asserted by defendants was not an affirmative defense, as the trial court incorrectly held, defendants failed to present testimony that the disbursements they received were in fact intended to be reimbursements for funds actually advanced on behalf of the trustee; that the statutory presumption of wrongful diversion of trust funds contained in subdivision 3 of section 79-a of the Lien Law was constitutional since it bore a rational relation to the fact presumed and the fact proved; that the individual defendants were personally liable for the receipt of the improper disbursements since they actually received the funds and participated in the transfers thereof; that the prosecution failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt the requisite culpable intent for the offense of making apparently sworn false statements; that the omission of a material fact from public offering statements was proven by sufficient evidence; that one count relating to misrepresentation of material facts in such offering statements must be reversed as to one defendant who was found not guilty on another count relating to the same statement, and, that charges relating to misappropriation of moneys advanced by purchasers of condominium units were supported by the evidence. With regard to the charges of making apparently sworn false statements it suffices to say that the prosecution failed to demonstrate beyond a reasonable doubt that the affidavits submitted to the lending institution, in order to secure a building construction loan, constituted a falsity.

Crimes -- Larceny -- Misappropriation of Trust Funds -- Presumption of Wrongful Diversion of Funds

2. Subdivision 3 of section 79-a of the Lien Law, which provides that the failure of a trustee to keep books or records as required by section 75 of such law shall be presumptive evidence that the trust funds were applied for a nontrust purpose, does not fall prey to any constitutional infirmity where the courts below treated this statutory presumption as only a permissible inference that defendants used trust funds for other than authorized trust purposes; the presumption does not relate to criminal intent and thus the prosecution was not relieved of proving defendants' guilt beyond a reasonable doubt and the statute did not work to shift the burden of proof to defendants; a rational basis exists between the fact proved (failure to keep records) and the fact presumed (applying trust funds for a nontrust purpose).

Jaffe v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 990; 409 N.E.2d 1002; 431 N.Y.S.2d 530; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2524


June 3, 1980, Argued  
June 26, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Defense of Laches

In a consolidated proceeding to compel the New York City Board of Education to reinstate petitioners' decedents as teachers as of February 1, 1967 and to retire them as of the dates of their deaths, which proceeding was brought in 1977 after the statutes under which decedents had been discharged in 1951 were held unconstitutional in 1967, and after petitioners filed claims for reinstatement in 1973 which were denied, an order of the Appellate Division, which dismissed the proceeding on the merits, is affirmed for the reasons stated in the memorandum thereat, which concluded that the causes of action of petitioners' decedents accrued in 1967; that the inordinate delay in asserting the claims for reinstatement constituted laches, and that when the equitable defense of laches is invoked in an article 78 proceeding in the nature of mandamus, proof [**3] of unexcused delay without more may be sufficient to sustain the defense.

 

253 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Benson Realty Corp. v. Beame


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 994; 409 N.E.2d 948; 431 N.Y.S.2d 475; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2526


June 4, 1980, Argued  
June 26, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, with costs to defendants, in accordance with the memorandum herein, and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realtors sought review of an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York) that modified the trial court's order declaring the New York City Rent Control Law unconstitutional and denying the motion of realtors, and the cross motion of defendants, mayor and related parties, for summary judgment by deleting the denial of the cross motion.


OVERVIEW: The appellate division found that the realtors failed to meet their burden of overcoming the presumption constitutionality attached to the rent control law. The court found, however, that the consequence of the realtors' failure to rebut the presumption was that the mayor and the related parties were entitled to a declaration of constitutionality. In so ruling, the court found that the realtors failed to show that there was no longer a need for rent control, noting that the housing authority had recently reviewed the issue, and had found there to be a continuing need. The court also rejected the realtors' suggestion that the law resulted in unlawful taking. The court found that the realtors generalized conclusions were insufficient to establish an unconstitutional taking. Finally, the court disposed of the realtors' challenge to the law based upon a collapse of administration. The court noted that, even if there had been a lack of administration of the law, there was no authority to support the position that misadministration could render a statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court modified the appellate division's order by substituting the appellate division's declaration and dismissal with the declaration that the rent control law was constitutional. As modified, the court affirmed the appellate division's order.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Presumption of Validity of Statute

1. In an action for a judgment declaring the New York City Rent Control Law unconstitutional, an order of the Appellate Division, which modified an order denying plaintiffs' and defendants' motions for summary judgment, by declaring that plaintiffs failed to rebut the presumption of constitutionality of the laws in question and by otherwise dismissing the complaint, is modified, by substituting a declaration that the New York City Rent Control Law is constitutional. Plaintiffs failed to rebut the presumption of constitutionality since they did not present evidence to demonstrate beyond a reasonable doubt that there is no factual basis for the legislative determination that there is a need for rent control or to demonstrate that there has been an unconstitutional taking of the property of any individual owner.

Constitutional Law -- Interpretation of Statute

2. There is no authority for the proposition that proof of maladministration or nonadministration of a statute may serve as the predicate for a judicial declaration that the statute is unconstitutional; the role of the judiciary is to enforce statutes and to rule on challenges to their constitutionality either on their face or as applied in accordance with their provisions, and any problems that result from pervasive nonenforcement are political questions for solution by the legislative or executive branches.

Bellanca v. New York State Liquor Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 524; 407 N.E.2d 460; 429 N.Y.S.2d 616; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2396


April 30, 1980, Argued  
June 10, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the owners of nightclubs, bars, and restaurants featuring topless dancing (owners), brought an action against defendant New York State Liquor Authority (authority), insofar as it prohibited topless dancing at premises licensed by the authority. The trial court granted summary judgment to the owners, and the appellate court affirmed. The authority appealed.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 106(6-a) prohibited topless dancing at premises licensed by the authority. The owners brought an action against the authority, and the trial court held that § 106(6-a) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that topless dancing was not inherently obscene but was a legally recognized form of expression. Topless dancing was entitled to at least minimal protection under the First Amendment. The court found that the state could not arbitrarily prohibit topless dancing at all places licensed to sell alcohol. There was nothing in the record to show that § 106(6-a) was rationally based on evidence demonstrating a need for the law. The court found nothing that could rationally support a conclusion that it was dangerous to mix alcohol and topless dancing in New York.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, which had affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the owners in their action against the authority to determine the constitutionality of topless dancing at premises licensed by the authority.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating Liquors -- Licenses -- Topless Dancing

Topless dancing is not inherently obscene and is a form of expression entitled to at least a minimum of protection under the First Amendment to the United States Constitution, although, since it involves conduct, it is subject to more restrictions than the more static arts; the State cannot prohibit topless dancing under all circumstances and neither may the State, under subdivision 6-a of section 106 of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, arbitrarily prohibit it at all places licensed to sell alcoholic beverages. Accordingly, since the State has failed to demonstrate that there is rational connection between the activity sought to be prohibited and the State's legitimate concern in controlling liquor consumption, the trial court properly declared subdivision 6-a unconstitutional as applied to topless dancing in licensed premises and, to that extent, enjoined its enforcement.

People ex rel. Douglas v. Vincent


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 901; 409 N.E.2d 990; 431 N.Y.S.2d 518; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2468


April 22, 1980, Argued  
June 10, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, without costs, in a memorandum.


HEADNOTES

Habeas Corpus -- When Remedy Appropriate

Where petitioner, claiming the trial court's charge on the defense of justification was inadequate, brought a habeas corpus proceeding challenging the legality of his detention, alleging, inter alia, ineffective assistance of appellate counsel, after a judgment convicting him of murder had been affirmed by the Appellate Division and leave to appeal had been denied by the Court of Appeals, an order of the Appellate Division which reversed a judgment of the Supreme Court granting the petition to the extent of directing that the petitioner be resentenced by the Monroe County Court, in order that his time to appeal might run anew, is affirmed on so much of the reasoning of the Appellate Division's opinion as concluded that petitioner's grievances were beyond habeas corpus relief. In addition, it is noted that even if there were merit to the petitioner's contention that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at trial or appeal, he would not be entitled to habeas corpus relief because the remedy he seeks would provide him a new trial or new appeal but not a direction that he be immediately released from custody. No view is expressed as to whether petitioner's claim of deprivation of effective appellate counsel may be heard in a proceeding in the nature of coram nobis.

People v. Shepard


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 640; 409 N.E.2d 840; 431 N.Y.S.2d 363; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2497


February 7, 1980, Argued  
June 6, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Appellate Term of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York) which affirmed a judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant possessed marihuana plants in his home. Defendant was charged with criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree. Defendant moved to dismiss the charge on the ground that the statute making marihuana possession illegal violated his right to privacy. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss and held that defendant had failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality that attached to all legislative enactments. Thus, the trial court found defendant guilty as charged and sentenced him to pay a fine. The appeals court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed holding that defendant's contention that the state could not constitutionally criminalize the possession and cultivation of personal use quantities of marihuana within the privacy of the home was without merit because the legislature did not make marihuana possession a constitutionally protected right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the state legislature did not make marihuana possession a constitutionally protected right.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Controlled Substances -- Possession of Marihuana for Personal Use

The conviction of a defendant found guilty of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree (Penal Law, § 220.03) in that he possessed at his home nine marihuana plants is affirmed; although there is disagreement regarding the effects of marihuana, a court does not have the right to substitute its own sense of what is a dangerous substance for the considered judgment of the Legislature. It would be inappropriate for a court to prematurely remove marihuana from the Legislature's consideration by classifying its personal possession as a constitutionally protected right.

 

257 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thomas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 467; 407 N.E.2d 430; 429 N.Y.S.2d 584; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2391


March 20, 1980, Argued  
June 5, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and case remitted to the Appellate Division, First Department, for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the trial court of three counts of murder in the second degree. The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the matter for a new trial. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder for stabbing and killing a woman and her children. The trial court informed the jury that the state had the burden of proving defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt and that the burden never shifted to defendant. With respect to the element of intent, the trial court emphasized that this was a matter for the jury to decide, and that in resolving the issue, they must consider the facts and all the surrounding circumstances. The trial court, however, also advised that the law stated that a person was presumed to intend the natural and probable consequences of his act and was presumed to intend that which he actually did. Defendant concededly did not object to this portion of the charge at trial. Nevertheless, he claimed that the trial court's reference to the "presumption" constituted reversible error. However, the court stated that defendant's failure to object could not have been excused on the ground that he was confronted at trial with a practice held or deemed to be valid which was only called into question by a decision announced while the case was on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remitted to the appellate court for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Appeal -- Matters Reviewable

Although no objection is necessary to preserve a point of law for appellate review when the procedure followed at trial was at basic variance with the mandate prescribed by Constitution or statute, as a general rule, claims of error involving Federal constitutional rights as well as State law which were not raised at trial may not be considered for the first time on appeal. Accordingly, where defendant was charged with murder in the second degree, which requires proof of intent to kill (Penal Law, § 125.25, subd 1), and the trial court instructed the jury, in general terms, that the People had the burden of proving defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt and that the burden never shifts to the defendant, but, with respect to the element of intent, the court stated that the law says that a person is presumed to intend the natural and probable consequences of his act and is presumed to intend that which he actually does, to which instruction defendant did not object, it was error for the Appellate Division to reverse defendant's conviction on the ground that the alleged error in the charge on the "presumption" presented a reviewable question of law despite the lack of objection inasmuch as the court's charge effectively absolved the People of the duty to prove an essential element of murder in the second degree, viz., intent to kill; when a court's specific instructions on the burden of proof properly place the burden on the People, a claim that a portion of the charge could, in the particular case, be interpreted as having a contrary effect, does not come within the narrow exception to the rule that objections to charge must be made at trial.

 

258 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Park of Edgewater, Inc. v. Joy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 946; 409 N.E.2d 931; 431 N.Y.S.2d 457; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2500


March 17, 1980, Argued; April 29, 1980, Reargued  
June 5, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, with costs, and the judgment of Supreme Court, New York County, reinstated in a memorandum.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city housing commissioner challenged a judgment of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which reversed a finding confirming the commissioner's determination that ground rents for respondent owner's property were not within rent decontrol provisions of state law.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought a rent decontrol order for its property, arguing that the transfer of a land lease allowed for such decontrol. However, on review, the court reversed the judgment of the lower appellate court and reinstated the trial court's finding confirming the city commissioner's determination that the property was not subject to state decontrol provisions. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that, under applicable law, rent decontrol did not attach where the lease transfer was to a family member of the prior lessees, such as in the case at issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's judgment and reinstated the judgment confirming the city commissioner's finding that the owner's property did not fall within the rent decontrol provisions of state law.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Control -- Vacancy Decontrol

In a proceeding to annul a determination of the Commissioner of the City of New York Housing Preservation and Development Administration, Office of Rent and Housing Maintenance, Rent Control Division, that ground rents for petitioner's property were not within a vacancy decontrol provision of section 2 (subd f, par [17]) of the New York City Rent and Eviction Regulations, an order of the Appellate Division, which reversed a judgment dismissing the petition and annulled the determination, is reversed, and the judgment of Supreme Court is reinstated. During the pendency of the appeal chapter 69 of the Laws of 1980 became law and sections 2 and 3 of that statute amended the Rent Control Law and related provisions of the Administrative Code of the City of New York, and since that statute provides that transfer to a member of the leaseholder's family did not decontrol the lease and the statute was made retroactive to July 1, 1971, the transfer in this case, having occurred to the leaseholder's son in 1975, had no bearing upon whether the property involved in this proceeding is controlled; since the issue of the constitutionality of the new statute was waived by the parties and only one parcel was involved in this proceeding, the constitutional question is not reached.

 

259 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Keeffe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 149; 405 N.E.2d 1012; 428 N.Y.S.2d 446; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2277


March 26, 1980, Argued  
May 1, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed defendant's second-degree larceny conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant became substitute counsel in a wrongful death action. After settlement, the previous counsel placed a lien on the proceeds for his fee. A subsequent order provided that the previous counsel would receive $ 2,500. When the amount in defendant's special account fell below $ 2,500, defendant was indicted and convicted of second-degree larceny. The appellate division affirmed. The court of appeals reversed. The order fixing previous counsel's fee did not give him property in or ownership of the money held by defendant in the special account as those terms were defined by N.Y. Penal Law § 155.00. Furthermore, the fact that the proceeds were in a special account did not make them trust funds held for previous counsel's benefit. Consequently, defendant's withdrawals from the special account did not constitute larceny.


OUTCOME: The order affirming defendant's second-degree larceny conviction was reversed, and that count of the indictment was dismissed. Defendant's depletion of special account did not constitute larceny from his client's previous counsel even though the balance was reduced to less than the amount owed to his client's previous counsel.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Larceny -- Funds Held in Attorney's Account

1. An attorney who holds in his special account the proceeds of settlement of a personal injury action is not guilty of larceny when his withdrawals from the special account reduce its balance to less than the amount to which his predecessor attorney has been held entitled as his share of the fee; the predecessor attorney did not by reason of the order fixing the amount of his fee have "property" in or ownership of the money held by the successor attorney (Penal Law, § 155.00), but rather had only a contract right to recover a fee and the fact that the proceeds were in a special or "attorney's" account did not make them trust funds held for the benefit of the outgoing attorney.

Motions and Orders -- Effect of Decision

2. Until its directions are embodied in an order or decree a decision has no legal significance.

Attorney and Client -- Attorney's Lien

3. With but two exceptions, the rendition of services by an attorney gives rise to nothing more than a contract claim by the attorney against his client; the exceptions are the attorney's retaining lien, which entitles the attorney to retain all papers, securities or money belonging to the client which comes into his possession until the amount of his fee is fixed and is paid, and the attorney's charging lien, which gives a lien upon the client's cause of action from the commencement of the action (or if a proper notice is served, prior to such commencement), and attaches to the judgment and the proceeds of the judgment and cannot be effected by settlement between the parties (Judiciary Law, §§ 475, 475-a). When by a retainer agreement the client expressly assigns a portion of the cause of action proceeds to his attorney the attorney acquires vested property interest which cannot subsequently be disturbed by the client or anyone claiming through or against the client, but absent express language of assignment, the attorney has no ownership or immediate right to possession and must obtain enforcement of his lien by appropriate order of the court in which the action is pending. An attorney's charging lien may be lost if he voluntarily withdraws or is discharged for misconduct, among other ways, and if an attorney is discharged without cause he will generally be allowed a charging lien upon the proceeds of the lawsuit, the amount to be determined on a quantum meruit basis at the conclusion of the case, and his fees will be made a charge included within the fees to which the incoming attorney will be entitled.

 

260 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Chesler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 203; 406 N.E.2d 455; 428 N.Y.S.2d 639; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2294


March 24, 1980, Argued  
May 1, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecutor sought review of a decision from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Fourth Judicial Department (New York), which reversed respondent criminal's convictions and held that the trial court erroneously charged that repayment under N.Y Lien Law § 79-a(2) was an affirmative defense to be established by respondent by a preponderance of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: A new trial had been granted after the intermediate appellate court had reversed respondent criminal's convictions for grand larceny in the second degree in violation of N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a on the grounds that the trial court had erroneously charged that the defense of repayment under N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a(2) was an affirmative defense to be shown by respondent. On review, appellant conceded that the trial court had erroneously charged the jury regarding the defense of repayment. The court agreed and held that appellant had the burden of proving the requisite criminal intent beyond a reasonable doubt in obtaining a conviction under N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a. The court affirmed and noted that any application of N.Y. Penal Law § 155.15, which made "good faith" an affirmative defense for the crime of larceny, in the prosecution of the new trial was a constitutionally impermissible shift of the burden of proof from appellant to respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of respondent criminal's convictions for grand larceny in the second degree, finding that it was error to charge the jury that respondent had the burden of establishing the defense of repayment by a preponderance of the evidence where it was an ordinary defense.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Larceny -- Defense

On a charge of larceny in violation of section 79-a of the Lien Law, a defense of actual repayment to creditors based on subdivision 2 of that section is an ordinary defense and not an affirmative defense. To the extent that the application of section 155.15 of the Penal Law would classify as an "affirmative defense" the related "good faith" defense based on the contention that even if the payments in question were not actually made to creditors as required by subdivision 2, defendant nonetheless in good faith believed them to be at the time, such application would be unconstitutional because it would shift the burden of proof to defendant.

 

261 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Uniformed Firefighters Asso. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


50 N.Y.2d 85; 405 N.E.2d 679; 428 N.Y.S.2d 197; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2271


March 20, 1980, Argued  
April 29, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an amended order and judgment granting plaintiff associations' motion for summary judgment, denying the city's motion for summary judgment, and declaring New York City Local Law No. 20 of 1978 invalid and enjoining its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the lower courts' judgments, holding that the city could not, through Local Law No. 20 of the Local Laws of 1978 (N.Y. City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ B49-4.0, B49-4.1, B49-4.2), make a residency requirement for municipal officers and employees applicable to members of its police, fire, correction, and sanitation departments because the law as applicable to those persons was inconsistent with exemptions from such requirements contained in N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 3(2), (2-a), (9); § 30(4), (4-a), (5). The court held that those sections could not be superseded by local law under municipal home rule because they did not relate to the property, affairs, or government of the city by "special law" under N.Y. Const. art IX, § 2. The court noted that while the structure and control of the municipal service departments could be considered of local concern within the meaning of municipal home rule, the residence of their members, unrelated to job performance or departmental organization, was a matter of state-wide concern not subject to municipal home rule. Thus, to the extent that Local Law No. 20 was inconsistent with the Public Officers Law, it could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower courts' orders which held that to the extent that Local Law No. 20 was inconsistent with the provisions of the Public Officers Law, it could not stand.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Residence of Municipal Employees of City of New York

New York City may not, through Local Law No. 20 of 1978 (Administrative Code of City of New York, §§ B49-4.0 -- B49-4.2), make a residency requirement for municipal officers and employees applicable to members of its police, fire, correction and sanitation departments, since the law as applicable to these persons is inconsistent with exemptions from municipal residency requirements contained in section 3 (subds 2, 2-a, 9) and section 30 (subds 4, 4-a, 5) of the Public Officers Law, which sections may not be superseded by local law under municipal home rule as they do not relate "to the property, affairs or government" of the city by "special law" (NY Const, art IX, § 2); the provisions of said statutes are not infirm because they may affect less than all cities, since what is required is that the classification be defined by conditions common to the class and related to the subject of the statute, and it has long been recognized that New York City and other large municipal centers might reasonably receive different treatment.

 

262 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Dolan v. Whalen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


49 N.Y.2d 991; 406 N.E.2d 1063; 429 N.Y.S.2d 169; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2347


March 18, 1980, Argued  
April 29, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which reversed a judgment of the lower court granting consolidation of the employee's proceeding, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, seeking sick leave at half pay with the employee's subsequent motion by way of order to show cause to compel his reinstatement, and dismissed the petition.


OVERVIEW: The employee became ill and was unable to work. He was informed that he had been granted sick leave at half pay for a period of time. Subsequently, he was terminated pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 73 since he had been continuously absent from his position due to his disability for a period of one year. The employee brought an proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review his termination. The trial court granted consolidation of the employee's article 78 proceeding with a subsequent motion by way of order to show cause to compel his reinstatement. The lower appellate court reversed. The court affirmed. It found his claim, that N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 73 was unconstitutional because it permitted termination without a hearing of an employee continuously absent from and unable to perform the duties of his position for one year or more by reason of a disability, meritless. A hearing was required only when there was some factual dispute impacting upon the employer's right to discharge. No hardship was demonstrated by the employee, and the many written statements by the employee and his physicians obviated any question that he was continuously disabled for the requisite period.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the employee's challenge to his termination from state employment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Termination of Employment

An order of the Appellate Division which reversed a judgment of the Supreme Court granting consolidation of petitioner's article 78 proceeding seeking sick leave at half pay with petitioner's subsequent motion by way of order to show cause to compel his reinstatement, declaring the attempted termination of petitioner's employment null and void, granting petitioner additional sick leave, and restoring him to his former position as Senior Attorney, and dismissed the petition, is affirmed. The record contains nothing to establish that petitioner is in fact a veteran protected by section 75 (subd 1, pars [a], [b]) of the Civil Service Law from termination of his position without a hearing. Nor does section 73 of the Civil Service Law unconstitutionally permit termination of an employee without a hearing, since only when there is some factual dispute impacting upon the employer's right to discharge is a hearing required by that section and that hearing may, in the absence of demonstrated serious hardship, be held posttermination; here no hardship was demonstrated and petitioner has obviated any question that he was continuously disabled for the requisite period. As to petitioner's claim that he was entitled to be reinstated on June 6, 1978 rather than August 1, 1978, his right to reinstatement depended under section 73 on his making application for a medical examination by a doctor selected by the department, and the statute did not give petitioner the right to fix the date of the examination and he has not shown what caused the department's failure to reinstate him prior to August 1, 1978 or whether or when he was in fact examined by a department doctor.

 

263 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Gootnick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


49 N.Y.2d 683; 404 N.E.2d 1318; 427 N.Y.S.2d 777; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2191


March 24, 1980, Argued  
April 24, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, with costs to respondents, and the matter remitted to Supreme Court, Allegany County, for the entry of judgment in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, board of education and individuals, sought review of an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Fourth Judicial Department (New York), which, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, dismissed their petition challenging the constitutionality of N.Y. Educ. Law § 3020-a.


OVERVIEW: The court converted the N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to a declaratory judgment action because an art. 78 proceeding could not be used to test the constitutionality of a legislative enactment. The individual appellants had standing because if the statute was unconstitutional, they could be removed for knowingly participating in arbitration before a panel unconstitutionally selected. N.Y. Educ. Law § 3020-a revised the procedure for the hearing of charges against a person enjoying the benefits of tenure, a procedure applicable to school districts and teachers throughout the state. The court held that it was a general law, not a private or local law, which was not prohibited under N.Y. Const. art. III, §§ 15 and 17. The court held that the fact that the American Arbitration Association was reimbursed for its administrative expenses in preparing the list of nominees, or that a person from its list was to be compensated, did not make the bill a grant of an exclusive franchise or a private bill because the association merely presented the names of individuals exceptionally qualified for service as chairman and appointment from the list was not made by the association.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by converting the proceeding into a declaratory action. The court affirmed the judgment as modified and remitted the matter to the trial court for the entry of judgment declaring the statute constitutional. The court dismissed the action as to the board of education for lack of standing.


HEADNOTES

Declaratory Judgment -- When Remedy Appropriate

1. A CPLR article 78 proceeding may not be used to test the constitutionality of a legislative enactment, as distinct from the constitutionality of its application; accordingly, such a proceeding brought to determine the constitutionality of section 3020-a of the Education Law, which requires that the chairman of a panel hearing charges against a tenured person be chosen from a list furnished by the American Arbitration Association, is converted to a declaratory judgment action.

Declaratory Judgments -- Evidence -- Presentation of Evidence

2. In a declaratory judgment action to determine the constitutionality of a statute, the factual data on which the claim of unconstitutionality is based is to be presented as evidence to the trial court, not as addenda to briefs submitted in the Court of Appeals.

Parties -- Standing

3. In a declaratory judgment action to determine the constitutionality of section 3020-a of the Education Law, which provides that the chairman of a panel hearing charges against a tenured person be chosen from a list furnished by the American Arbitration Association, the individual members of a board of education have standing to sue, although the board does not, because, if the statute is found unconstitutional, they can be removed for knowingly participating in an arbitration before a panel unconstitutionally selected.

Schools -- Panel to Hear Charges against Tenured Person -- Appointment of Chairman from List Prepared by American Arbitration Association

4. Section 3020-a of the Education Law, as amended by chapter 82 of the Laws of 1977, which provides that the chairman of a panel hearing charges against a tenured person be chosen from a list furnished by the American Arbitration Association, is not unconstitutional as a private bill granting an exclusive franchise (NY Const, art III, § 17), since the bill, which revised the State-wide procedure for the hearing of charges against a tenured person, was clearly a general law, and the fact that the association was reimbursed for its administrative expenses in preparing the list, or that a person from its list is to be compensated at the rates usually paid him for his services as an arbiter for the association, does not make the law a grant of an exclusive franchise or a private bill; the association merely presents, on an objective and nonpartisan basis, the names of individuals exceptionally qualified by prior service in the field of adversarial hearings for service as chairman of a hearing panel under section 3020-a, and appointment from the list is not made by the association.

 

264 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Golden v. Koch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


49 N.Y.2d 690; 404 N.E.2d 1321; 427 N.Y.S.2d 780; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2192


February 11, 1980, Argued  
April 3, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city counsel president and board members, sought review of an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), that reversed the trial court's order granting them summary judgment, and granted respondent mayor summary judgment, in the declaratory judgment action of the city counsel president and board members, pursuant to New York City, N.Y., Charter § 120.


OVERVIEW: The city counsel president and the board members sought a declaration that the mayor was not entitled to vote as a member of the board of estimates on budget modifications he proposed. The city counsel president and the board members argued that § 120, which prohibited the mayor from voting on the budget, also applied to any modifications to the budget. At the outset, the court rejected the "careful and intelligent voter" standard employed by the appellate division to review the language of the city charter, and applied traditional rules of statutory construction. Applying that standard, the court found that the restrictions on the mayor's voting power under § 120 only applied to the approval of the original budget. The court noted that to rule otherwise would have rendered the enumerated instances in New York City, N.Y., Charter § 124(f) wherein the mayor's voting power was specifically restricted meaningless. Additionally, the court noted that such an interpretation was consistent with the rule of statutory construction that created an inference that what was omitted was intended to be omitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate division's order reversing the trial court's order granting the city counsel president and board members summary judgment, and granted the mayor summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Statutes -- Construction -- Publicly Approved Provisions

Publicly approved provisions of law should be interpreted by applying the traditionally accepted standards of statutory construction, rather than by seeking the meaning which the words would convey to an "intelligent, careful voter". Accordingly, as said traditionally accepted standards require that the New York City Charter be read as a whole and that each word in the charter be considered in arriving at its meaning, the restrictions upon the voting power of the Mayor of the City of New York on budgetary matters contained in subdivision d of section 120 of the revised charter should be limited to barring his participation in the approval of the original budget, since, to read that section as applying to subsequent budget modifications undertaken pursuant to subdivision b of section 124 would render the specific incorporation of section 120 in a selected few of the modification provisions in subdivision f of section 124 meaningless; it has long been held that where a statute describes the particular situations in which it is to apply, an irrefutable inference must be drawn that what is omitted or not included was intended to be omitted or excluded.

County of Oneida v. Berle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


49 N.Y.2d 515; 404 N.E.2d 133; 427 N.Y.S.2d 407; 1980 N.Y. LEXIS 2171


February 13, 1980, Argued  
April 1, 1980, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order, insofar as appealed from, modified, with costs to petitioners, in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review from a decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Fourth Judicial Department (New York), which unanimously affirmed a judgment granting a petition to restore $ 7 million of appropriated funds impounded by the Governor and the Director of the Budget to the budget of the Department of Environmental Conservation and ordering that the moneys so appropriated be dispersed in municipalities pursuant to law.


OVERVIEW: The appellate division affirmed a judgment granting a petition to restore $ 7 million of appropriated funds impounded by the Governor and the Director of the Budget to the budget of the Department of Environmental Conservation and ordering that the moneys so appropriated be dispersed in municipalities pursuant to law. Appellants sought review from the decision. On appeal, the court stated that, however, laudable its goals, the executive branch could not override enactments which had emerged from the lawmaking process. It was required to implement policy declarations of the legislature, unless vetoed or judicially invalidated. Under the Idaho Constitution, the executive possessed no express or inherent power, based upon its view of sound fiscal policy, to impound funds which had been appropriated by the legislature. The court modified the order of the appellate division to the extent of converting the proceeding into an action seeking declaratory relief. The court entered judgment declaring that the impoundment of $ 7 million of the appropriation was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the appellate division to the extent of converting the proceeding into an action seeking declaratory relief, and entered judgment declaring that the impoundment of $ 7 million of the appropriation was unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

State -- Budget

1. Although the Governor has a constitutional obligation to propose a balanced budget, the Governor, as the Chief Executive Officer of the State, is not obliged to maintain a balanced budget throughout the fiscal year, nor does he possess implied constitutional power to reduce duly enacted appropriations in order to attain that goal. Accordingly, the State Director of the Budget, as acting agent of the Governor, may not refuse to spend $ 7 million appropriated by the Legislature to aid municipalities in operating and maintaining sewage treatment works (L 1976, ch 53) in an effort to reduce State spending, where said appropriation statute conferred no discretionary authority upon the director to disapprove otherwise proper expenditures; a duly enacted statute, once passed, cannot be changed or varied according to the whim or caprice of any officer, board or individual, but remains fixed until repealed or amended by the Legislature.

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Mandamus

2. Where, because of a constitutional provision that states that no moneys shall ever be paid out of the State treasury except in pursuance of an appropriation by law within two years after the passage of such appropriation act (NY Const, art VII, § 7), it can no longer be said that respondents State officers are under a legal duty, which is so clear as not to admit of reasonable doubt or controversy, to allocate certain moneys appropriated by the Legislature more than two years prior to the final appeal on the allocation issue, mandamus would no longer be an appropriate remedy and, accordingly, said proceeding is converted from a CPLR article 78 proceeding in the nature of mandamus into a declaratory judgment action ( CPLR 103, subd [c]).

Fairbank Farms, Inc. v. Kasza

HEADNOTES

Administrative Law -- Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies

In a proceeding to prohibit sales tax examiners from assessing an additional sales tax liability on certain corporate transactions occasioned by a change in corporate accounting methods after a requested ruling by the Instructions and Interpretations Unit of the New York State Department of Taxation and Finance informed the corporation that the accounting change would not result in additional tax, an order of the Appellate Division, which reversed a judgment of the Supreme Court granting an order of prohibition [**3] and dismissed the proceeding, is affirmed for the reasons stated in the memorandum at the Appellate Division, which concluded that since no final determination had been reached by the tax commission the corporation had failed to exhaust its administrative remedies as required by sections 1138 and 1140 of the Tax Law, and inasmuch as there was no challenge to the taxing authority's jurisdiction on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional, there must be compliance with the method of review prescribed in the Tax Law.
